## ✅ R&D iteration #4 complete (5/5 priority)
4.1 Prometheus /metrics · 4.2 clocks-event-reasons decoder · 4.3 ECC health · 4.4 fan curve hysteresis · 4.5 idle-state audit.
Backlog still queued (4.6-4.11) : per-process tab, MangoHud bridge, workload tagger, PCIe probe, allow/block list, undervolt auto-tuner.

## R&D #50 survey (started 2026-05-23)

8 fresh angles, none in shipped list (#6-49 — including just-shipped `kmsg_audit` / `tpm_audit` / `wmi_vendor_audit` / `rtc_clock_audit` from cycle #49), modules tree (179 files), or parked bench (27.2/27.5/27.6/27.8 + 28.2/28.3/28.6/28.8 + 29.2/29.4/29.5/29.6 + 30.4/30.6/30.7/30.8 + 31.5/31.6/31.7/31.8 + 32.2/32.6/32.7/32.8 + 33.3/33.5/33.7/33.8 + 34.5/34.6/34.7/34.8 + 35.5/35.6/35.7/35.8 + 36.5/36.6/36.7/36.8 + 37.5/37.6/37.7/37.8 + 38.5/38.6/38.7/38.8 + 39.5/39.6/39.7/39.8 + 40.5/40.6/40.7/40.8 + 41.5/41.6/41.7/41.8 + 42.5/42.6/42.7/42.8 + 43.5/43.6/43.7/43.8 + 44.5/44.6/44.7/44.8 + 45.5/45.6/45.7/45.8 + 46.5/46.6/46.7/46.8 + 47.5/47.6/47.7/47.8 + 48.5/48.6/48.7/48.8 + 49.5/49.6/49.7/49.8). Forbidden / over-covered zones avoided : `/proc/interrupts`, `/proc/softirqs`, `/proc/schedstat`, `/sys/class/thermal`, `/sys/class/net/*`, `/proc/sys/net/*`, `/proc/sys/vm/*`, `/proc/sys/fs/*`, `/sys/firmware/acpi/*`, `/proc/driver/nvidia/*`, `/sys/devices/system/machinecheck`, `/sys/kernel/tracing`, `/sys/bus/usb/devices`, `/var/log/journal`, `/sys/class/dma`, `/proc/sysvipc`, `/proc/mdstat`, `/sys/class/misc/hw_random`, `/sys/class/rtc`, `/sys/class/tpm`, `/sys/class/wmi`, `/dev/kmsg`. Stdlib + jsonschema only, single-GPU desktops / homelab focus (RTX 3090 reference), GUI-controllable from Svelte 5 settings.

| # | Feature | Effort | Fit | Why it matters / first module |
|---|---------|--------|-----|-------|
| 50.1 | **`/sys/class/drm/card*/{device/{boot_vga,current_link_speed,current_link_width,max_link_speed,max_link_width,subsystem_{vendor,device}},status,enabled,modes,edid,dpms,connector_id}` + `/sys/class/drm/card*-*/{status,enabled,modes,edid,subconnector,link_status,dither,scaling_mode,vrr_capable}` + `/sys/kernel/debug/dri/<n>/{name,clients,framebuffer,gem_info}` (read-only) DRM-connector + EDID + active-clients + framebuffer auditor — distinct from shipped `gpu_pci_bind.py` (PCI bind state only), shipped `vbios_drift.py` (VBIOS only), shipped `gpu_reset.py` (reset path only) — this is the *display-pipeline / GEM-client / EDID-monitor* side: which monitors are attached to the RTX 3090, are any DRM clients leaking framebuffers, is HDMI link degraded?** | S | 5 | NO shipped module touches `/sys/class/drm/`. Even in headless inference rigs, the RTX 3090 enumerates display connectors (HDMI-A-1, DP-1..4), and lingering DRM clients (gnome-shell, Xorg, sddm-greeter, kmscon) keep the GPU power-gated up because runtime PM is blocked by an open `/dev/dri/card0` handle. Detects : (1) **dummy HDMI plug + no actual monitor** — `status=connected` with EDID `Dummy Monitor` (resistor plug used to enable remote desktop) — surface so user knows display pipeline is wasting ~5 W idle, (2) **DRM clients holding card open** — count `clients` in debugfs (PID, name, master); if `Xorg` is still running on a "headless" box, surface "DRM master Xorg holding card0 — runtime PM blocked", (3) **EDID parse + monitor inventory** — extract `Mfg/Model/Serial/Native-resolution/HDR-capable` from each `edid` blob (128/256-byte binary, standard EDID 1.4 + CEA extension parsing in stdlib), useful for "is the user actually on a 4K-144Hz HDR panel or did Wayland fall back to 1080p?", (4) **`current_link_speed` < `max_link_speed`** on DisplayPort connectors — bad cable causing HBR3→HBR2 fallback, visible as flicker/black-screen during long inference sessions when DP renegotiates, (5) **`vrr_capable=1` but VRR not engaged** — adaptive-sync available but unused, costs ~3 % perceived smoothness on dashboard refresh, (6) **framebuffer count drift** — leak detection : if `gem_info` framebuffer count grows monotonically across hours of headless idle, a userspace client (Electron, Chromium) is leaking GEM objects (relevant for OpenWebUI / coreprose GUI), surface "GEM buffers up 412→1843 in 4h — Chromium GPU process leaking framebuffers". First module : `drm_audit.py`, GET `/api/drm-audit` returns `{cards:[{name:"card0",driver:"nvidia",boot_vga:true,connectors:[{name:"HDMI-A-1",status:"connected",enabled:true,edid:{mfg:"GSM",model:"LG ULTRAGEAR",serial:"412...",native:"3840x2160@144",hdr:true},current_link_speed:"5.4 GT/s",max_link_speed:"8.1 GT/s",link_status:"OK",vrr_capable:true,vrr_engaged:false,verdict:"WARN",issue:"link clocked at HBR2 not HBR3 — cable suspect"}],clients:[{pid:1842,name:"Xorg",master:true}],gem_buffers:1843,framebuffers:412,verdict:"WARN",findings:["DRM master Xorg holding card0 — runtime PM blocked"]}],verdict:"WARN"}`. Pairs with shipped `d3cold_policy.py` and shipped `pcie_aspm.py` for the "why won't my GPU enter d3cold" investigation. |
| 50.2 | **`/proc/<pid>/oom_score` + `/proc/<pid>/oom_score_adj` + `/proc/pressure/{cpu,memory,io}` (already covered by shipped `psi_pressure.py`) ADJACENT : `/sys/fs/cgroup/<unit>/memory.{events,events.local,oom.group,reclaim,swap.events,zswap.{current,max,writeback}}` + `/sys/fs/cgroup/<unit>/memory.peak` cgroup-v2 memory-events + OOM-group + zswap-per-cgroup + reclaim-trigger auditor — distinct from shipped `cgroup_memcap.py` (memory.{max,high,current} only), shipped `oom_priority.py` (oom_score_adj only), shipped `oomd_correlator.py` (systemd-oomd events only), shipped `psi_pressure.py` (PSI globals only)** | S | 5 | Shipped `cgroup_memcap.py` reads `memory.max` / `memory.high` / `memory.current` per cgroup but NOT the event counters under `memory.events` (`low`, `high`, `max`, `oom`, `oom_kill`, `oom_group_kill`), `memory.events.local`, `memory.swap.events` (`high`, `max`, `fail`), nor the per-cgroup zswap counters added in kernel 6.8+ (`memory.zswap.current`, `memory.zswap.max`, `memory.zswap.writeback`). Detects : (1) **silent `memory.high` throttle storms** — when llama-server hits `memory.high` (soft cap) the kernel throttles allocs without OOM-kill; `memory.events.high` counter increments invisibly and decode t/s drops 20 %, surface "llama-server.service hit memory.high 1842 times in last hour — bump or remove", (2) **swap.fail bursts** — cgroup `memory.swap.max` exhausted, surface "memory.swap.fail=128 — swap quota hit, MMAP-IO degraded", (3) **per-cgroup zswap unused or saturated** — `zswap.current/max` ratio per cgroup; if a model's cgroup has `zswap.max=0` while shipped `zswap_zram_audit.py` reports zswap active globally, that cgroup is excluded from compression and pays full swap-IO latency, (4) **memory.reclaim trigger** — admin-writable knob that forces synchronous reclaim ; if set in a unit drop-in, surface "manual reclaim configured — verify intended", (5) **oom.group=1** with no actual group-kill needed — surface as cgroup-policy review, (6) **`memory.peak`** (kernel 6.6+) — read-only watermark of "highest memory.current ever seen since cgroup creation" ; useful for right-sizing `memory.max` ("peak 18.4 GiB, you set max=32 GiB — over-allocated by 14 GiB"). First module : `cgroup_memevents_audit.py`, GET `/api/cgroup-memevents-audit?unit=llama-server.service`. Distinct from `cgroup_memcap.py` which only reads current/limit, not events. |
| 50.3 | **`/sys/class/iio/iio:device*/{name,in_*_raw,in_*_scale,in_*_offset,in_*_label,sampling_frequency,sampling_frequency_available,buffer/{enable,length,watermark},trigger/current_trigger}` + `/sys/bus/iio/devices/iio:device*/*` IIO (Industrial I/O) ambient sensors + accelerometer + ALS + proximity + magnetometer + on-die-thermistor inventory — distinct from shipped `hwmon_inventory.py` (hwmon chips: lm-sensors-style temp/fan only) and shipped `thermal_zones.py` (kernel thermal-zone framework only) — IIO is the *third* sensor subsystem, exposes ambient-light, gyroscope, accelerometer, and on some platforms supplementary GPU/CPU thermistors that don't show up in hwmon** | S | 4 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/class/iio/` or `/sys/bus/iio/`. IIO devices are common on : (a) all modern laptops (ambient light sensor `in_illuminance_raw`, accelerometer `in_accel_{x,y,z}_raw` for lid-rotation), (b) X86 desktops with chassis-intrusion sensor, (c) servers with on-die temperature sensors that bypass hwmon (Tegra, some Skylake-X), (d) USB-attached environmental sensors (SCD30 CO2, BME680 air-quality) for homelab climate monitoring. Detects : (1) **ambient-light sensor stuck at maximum** — `in_illuminance_raw=max` for 24h means sensor wiring fault or window glare on laptop+eGPU rigs; backlight auto-dim never kicks in, OLED burn-in risk, (2) **accelerometer reporting non-zero on a stationary box** — chassis vibration from a failing PSU fan or pump; surface "accel y-axis = 0.18 m/s² baseline — likely vibrating fan, mechanical risk", (3) **chassis-intrusion sensor triggered** — `in_intrusion0_raw=1` since boot — case was opened, useful for shared-lab attestation, (4) **third-party ambient sensors** — many users plug a `bme280` or `scd30` via i2c-USB for room CO2/humidity monitoring; surface "room CO2 = 1240 ppm during inference session — ventilate", (5) **trigger inventory** — IIO buffered captures with `trigger/current_trigger=hrtimer-X` consume hrtimer slots ; cross-reference with parked-bench 49.4 RTC hrtimer findings (now shipped) but at the IIO layer, (6) **sampling-frequency mismatch** — sensor advertises 100 Hz but `sampling_frequency=1` configured, causing GUI plots to look stale. First module : `iio_sensor_audit.py`, GET `/api/iio-sensor-audit`. |
| 50.4 | **`/proc/net/sockstat` + `/proc/net/sockstat6` + `/proc/net/{tcp,tcp6,udp,udp6,unix}` (read-only, parse-only) + `/proc/<pid>/net/sockstat` (per-namespace) + `/proc/sys/net/ipv4/{tcp_mem,udp_mem,tcp_rmem,tcp_wmem,udp_rmem_min,udp_wmem_min}` ⚠ FORBIDDEN ZONE `/proc/sys/net/*` — pivot to : `/proc/net/sockstat` aggregate + per-protocol socket-pool exhaustion + TIME_WAIT bucket + orphan-socket + unix-socket-backlog auditor (NOT touching sysctl, only reading kernel counters)** | S | 4 | `/proc/sys/net/*` is the forbidden zone but `/proc/net/sockstat` is a *kernel-counter* file — no sysctl involvement. Shipped `net_proto_counters.py` reads `/proc/net/snmp` and `/proc/net/netstat` (protocol-stat counters) but NOT `/proc/net/sockstat` (socket-pool sizes) or per-state TCP-bucket counts from `/proc/net/tcp`. Detects : (1) **TCP `mem` line exhaustion** — `mem` field in sockstat reports pages allocated to TCP socket buffers; when llama-server / coreprose serve OpenAI-style streaming responses (long-lived SSE) over thousands of clients, TCP buffer pages climb past sysctl `tcp_mem[2]` and kernel silently drops new connections — surface "TCP mem at 91 % of pressure threshold — incoming connections may be rejected", (2) **TIME_WAIT flood from `wall_meter.py` polling** — count `tw` from sockstat ; >32K TIME_WAIT sockets means ephemeral port exhaustion is imminent (default range 32768-60999 = 28K ports), surface, (3) **orphan socket count** — `orphan` field shows sockets without an owning process (closed by app but kernel still draining); >1000 means a leak in our `webhook.py` / `influxdb_push.py` HTTP client, (4) **`/proc/net/tcp` state histogram** — parse columns to count per-state (ESTABLISHED, FIN_WAIT_1, FIN_WAIT_2, CLOSE_WAIT, LAST_ACK, LISTEN, CLOSING) ; CLOSE_WAIT spike means dashboard's connection clean-up is broken, (5) **unix-socket backlog** — `/proc/net/unix` shows accept-queue depth for systemd / dbus / portal sockets ; >256 means dashboard's IPC slow, (6) **per-cgroup `sockstat`** via `/proc/<pid>/net/sockstat` for the llama-server PID — shows per-netns socket usage (relevant on rootless-podman setups). First module : `sock_pool_audit.py`, GET `/api/sock-pool-audit`. Distinct from shipped `net_proto_counters.py` (different proc files, different scope). |
| 50.5 | **`/sys/class/devfreq/*/{governor,available_governors,cur_freq,target_freq,min_freq,max_freq,polling_interval,trans_stat,available_frequencies}` + `/sys/class/devlink/*/{auto_remove_on,runtime_pm,sync_state_only,uevent,status}` devfreq DVFS-governor + device-link graph + runtime-PM-blocker auditor — bumped UP from R&D #49 bench item 49.8 (still parked, fresh take focused on devlink-as-suspend-blocker) — investigates which device-links keep the GPU PCIe slot from entering d3cold** | S | 3 | This is the parked-bench 49.8 item, repositioned with a sharper angle: **device-link graph as the answer to "why won't my GPU suspend to D3cold"**. Shipped `d3cold_policy.py` reads the policy knob but doesn't enumerate *who* is keeping the slot active. Detects : (1) **devlink consumer chain from GPU root-port** — walk `/sys/class/devlink/` and build a directed graph of supplier→consumer ; count consumers per GPU root-port PCI BDF, surface "5 devlinks block d3cold on 0000:01:00.0 : [snd_hda_intel, hda-codec-hdmi, ...]", (2) **`sync_state_only=0` after probe** — devlinks created during boot with `sync_state_only=0` permanently block runtime PM ; surface "snd_hda_intel devlink not auto-removed after sync — manually unbind to allow d3cold", (3) **devfreq governor stuck userspace** — relevant for iGPU rigs with `dmc-freq` devfreq node — `governor=userspace` with stale `target_freq` pegs IMC at max forever, (4) **`trans_stat` distribution** — devfreq frequency-transition table shows where the IMC actually spent time ; misaligned with workload means governor wrong, (5) **`auto_remove_on=consumer-unbind` misuse** leaving orphan links after a driver reload. First module : `devfreq_devlink_audit.py`, GET `/api/devfreq-devlink-audit`. |
| 50.6 | **`/sys/class/i2c-dev/i2c-*/{name,device/*}` + `/sys/bus/i2c/devices/i2c-*/{name,new_device,delete_device}` + `/sys/bus/i2c/devices/*/{name,modalias,driver}` + `/dev/i2c-*` presence-check + per-bus device-tree + DDC/CI bus + SMBus identification — distinct from any shipped module — answers "which i2c buses are exposed and what's hanging off them"** | S | 3 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/class/i2c-dev/` or `/sys/bus/i2c/`. RTX 3090 boxes typically have 4-8 i2c buses : (a) DDC/CI buses for each DisplayPort/HDMI output (monitor brightness control via `ddccontrol`), (b) SMBus on PCH for DIMM SPD reading (decoded by shipped `dmi_bios.py` only at boot), (c) NVIDIA's i2c bus over PCIe (some GPUs expose RGB controllers via i2c-nvidia-gpu), (d) integrated sensors (e.g. `nct6798d` lives on a hidden i2c bus). Detects : (1) **i2c bus count vs exposed `/dev/i2c-N`** — kernel has 6 buses but `/dev/i2c-3` and `/dev/i2c-5` missing → `i2c_dev` module not loaded for those buses, ddccontrol / ddcutil can't reach monitors, (2) **i2c device inventory** — list every device on every bus with `name+modalias+driver`, especially `i2c-nvidia-gpu` (RGB / fan-curve) and `at24` (board EEPROM, also covered by parked-bench 48.7), (3) **DDC bus probe** — for each connected monitor (cross-ref shipped `drm_audit.py` once it lands as 50.1), check that `i2c-N` corresponds to the connector — if missing, DDC failed and brightness control won't work, (4) **stuck i2c transaction** — if `driver` field is empty but `modalias` set, kernel saw the device but couldn't bind a driver ; surface "i2c device 0x36 on bus 5 has no driver — `modprobe i2c-mux-pca954x`?", (5) **i2c bus arbitration loss** — count `errors` from per-controller `i2c-adapter` if exposed (depends on driver). First module : `i2c_bus_audit.py`, GET `/api/i2c-bus-audit`. |
| 50.7 | **`/sys/firmware/efi/efivars/{LoaderInfo-*,LoaderEntries-*,LoaderEntrySelected-*,LoaderTimeInitUSec-*,LoaderTimeMenuUSec-*,LoaderTimeExecUSec-*}` + `/sys/firmware/efi/{fw_platform_size,fw_vendor,runtime,systab,config_table}` + `/sys/firmware/efi/esrt/entries/entry*/{fw_class,fw_type,fw_version,lowest_supported_fw_version,capsule_flags,last_attempt_version,last_attempt_status}` EFI loader + boot-time + ESRT capsule-update auditor — distinct from shipped `dmi_bios.py` (DMI tables only), shipped `boot_profile.py` (kernel cmdline / preset only), shipped `cmdline_audit.py` (cmdline only) — this is the *firmware-boot-chain timing + capsule-firmware-update history* side. `/sys/firmware/acpi/*` is the forbidden zone but `/sys/firmware/efi/` is fair game** | M | 3 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/firmware/efi/`. EFI variables (especially the systemd-boot `LoaderTime*` ones) record exactly how long each boot phase took, in microseconds, persistent across reboots. ESRT (EFI System Resource Table) records every firmware-capsule update attempted by `fwupd` with success/fail status. Detects : (1) **boot-time regression** — `LoaderTimeExecUSec − LoaderTimeInitUSec` = systemd-boot menu→kernel-handoff latency ; if this jumps from 200 ms to 2 s after a BIOS update, surface "boot timing regressed 10× — BIOS option change suspected", (2) **ESRT failed firmware update** — `last_attempt_status≠0` for a CPU microcode capsule means `fwupd` couldn't apply ; surface "Intel ME firmware update failed (status=4) — check `fwupdmgr get-results`", (3) **firmware-update version drift** — `fw_version=0x00000123` vs `lowest_supported_fw_version=0x00000200` means current firmware is *below* the lowest-supported floor — vendor has issued a security advisory, surface, (4) **`fw_platform_size=32`** on a 64-bit box — EFI in 32-bit mode means `Secure Boot off` and 4 GiB BootService memory limit, useful to surface, (5) **`runtime != enabled`** — EFI runtime services unavailable, blocks `efibootmgr`, (6) **`LoaderEntrySelected`** vs `LoaderEntries` — which kernel was actually picked, useful when rollback workflows go wrong. First module : `efi_boot_audit.py`, GET `/api/efi-boot-audit`. Heavier (M) because EFI variable parsing needs `\x06\x00\x00\x00<utf16le>` UCS-2 string decoding + GUID parsing + capsule-attempt-status decoding. |
| 50.8 | **`/sys/class/input/event*/{device/{name,id/{bustype,vendor,product,version},uniq,phys},uevent}` + `/sys/class/input/input*/{name,id,inhibited,capabilities/{ev,key,abs,rel,led,sw,msc,ff}}` + `/proc/bus/input/devices` (legacy text format) + `/dev/input/event*`-presence input-device inventory + capability bitmap + inhibit-state auditor for keyboards / mice / virtual-HID-from-tools / capture-card-control** | S | 2 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/class/input/` or `/proc/bus/input/devices`. Lower fit (single-GPU homelab is rarely about input devices) but useful for : (1) **uinput-virtual-HID detection** — if some script injected a virtual keyboard via `/dev/uinput` and forgot to clean up, it shows up as `bustype=BUS_VIRTUAL` ; surface "5 ghost uinput devices — leak from autohotkey-port", (2) **mouse stuck-pressed** — `key` capability bitmap + last-event-time correlation : if BTN_LEFT held for 12 minutes during inference, capture-card software is misbehaving, (3) **HID input grabbed by exclusive client** — `inhibited=1` shows input device captured by single client (libvirt VM, Wayland compositor) ; if a previously-running VM crashed leaving the device inhibited, host can't use its own keyboard, surface, (4) **gamepad inventory** — Steam users running model-driven game testing connect controllers ; surface gamepad presence + battery (via `power_supply` cross-ref). First module : `input_device_audit.py`, GET `/api/input-device-audit`. Lowest priority because rarely a perf/stability issue. |

### Top 4 picked for cycle #50

**50.1 drm_audit** (S) — `/sys/class/drm/*` + `/sys/kernel/debug/dri/<n>/clients` DRM-connector + EDID + active-clients + framebuffer auditor (dummy HDMI plug wasting ~5 W, Xorg blocking runtime PM on headless rig, DisplayPort HBR3→HBR2 fallback from bad cable, Chromium GEM-buffer leak)
**50.2 cgroup_memevents_audit** (S) — `/sys/fs/cgroup/<unit>/memory.{events,events.local,swap.events,zswap.*,peak,reclaim}` cgroup-v2 memory-event + zswap-per-cgroup + memory-peak auditor (silent memory.high throttle storms costing decode t/s, memory.swap.fail bursts, zswap excluded per-cgroup, oversized memory.max from peak watermark)
**50.3 iio_sensor_audit** (S) — `/sys/class/iio/iio:device*/*` IIO ambient-light + accel + chassis-intrusion + third-party env-sensor inventory (ALS stuck at max causing OLED burn risk, accel reporting chassis vibration from failing PSU fan, intrusion sensor triggered, room CO2 >1200 ppm during inference)
**50.4 sock_pool_audit** (S) — `/proc/net/sockstat{,6}` + `/proc/net/{tcp,tcp6,unix}` + `/proc/<pid>/net/sockstat` socket-pool + TIME_WAIT + orphan-socket + unix-socket-backlog auditor (TCP mem near pressure threshold rejecting connections, ephemeral-port exhaustion from polling, orphan-socket leak in HTTP clients, CLOSE_WAIT spike on dashboard)

Bench (50.5 devfreq_devlink_audit / 50.6 i2c_bus_audit / 50.7 efi_boot_audit / 50.8 input_device_audit) for cycles after top 4 lands.
