## R&D #49 survey (started 2026-05-23)

8 fresh angles, none in shipped list (#6-48 — including just-shipped `ftrace_audit` / `usb_topology_audit` / `dma_audit` / `journal_audit` from cycle #48), modules tree (175 files), or parked bench (27.2/27.5/27.6/27.8 + 28.2/28.3/28.6/28.8 + 29.2/29.4/29.5/29.6 + 30.4/30.6/30.7/30.8 + 31.5/31.6/31.7/31.8 + 32.2/32.6/32.7/32.8 + 33.3/33.5/33.7/33.8 + 34.5/34.6/34.7/34.8 + 35.5/35.6/35.7/35.8 + 36.5/36.6/36.7/36.8 + 37.5/37.6/37.7/37.8 + 38.5/38.6/38.7/38.8 + 39.5/39.6/39.7/39.8 + 40.5/40.6/40.7/40.8 + 41.5/41.6/41.7/41.8 + 42.5/42.6/42.7/42.8 + 43.5/43.6/43.7/43.8 + 44.5/44.6/44.7/44.8 + 45.5/45.6/45.7/45.8 + 46.5/46.6/46.7/46.8 + 47.5/47.6/47.7/47.8 + 48.5/48.6/48.7/48.8). Forbidden / over-covered zones avoided : `/proc/interrupts`, `/proc/softirqs`, `/proc/schedstat`, `/sys/class/thermal`, `/sys/class/net/*`, `/proc/sys/net/*`, `/proc/sys/vm/*`, `/proc/sys/fs/*`, `/sys/firmware/acpi/*`, `/proc/driver/nvidia/*`, `/sys/devices/system/machinecheck`, `/sys/kernel/tracing`, `/sys/bus/usb/devices`, `/var/log/journal`, `/sys/class/dma`, `/proc/sysvipc`, `/proc/mdstat`, `/sys/class/misc/hw_random`. Stdlib + jsonschema only, single-GPU desktops / homelab focus (RTX 3090 reference), GUI-controllable from Svelte 5 settings.

| # | Feature | Effort | Fit | Why it matters / first module |
|---|---------|--------|-----|-------|
| 49.1 | **`/dev/kmsg` (read, non-blocking) + `/sys/kernel/printk{,_devkmsg,_ratelimit*}` + `/proc/sys/kernel/{printk,printk_devkmsg,printk_ratelimit,printk_ratelimit_burst,dmesg_restrict,kptr_restrict}` ring-buffer live-tail + facility/priority histogram + ratelimit-drop + restriction-policy auditor — distinct from shipped `journal_audit.py` (binary journal files only), shipped `nvrm_tail.py` (only filters `nvrm:`/`NVRM:` lines), shipped `xid_decoder.py` (XID strings only)** | S | 5 | NO shipped module reads `/dev/kmsg` directly — `journal_audit.py` parses the persisted `/var/log/journal/*.journal` but if `Storage=volatile` or journald hasn't flushed yet, the ring-buffer is the only source. `/dev/kmsg` exposes the kernel ring with `<priority>,<seq>,<timestamp_us>,<flags>;<message>\nKEY=value\n...` structured records readable in one stdlib `os.read()` per record (non-blocking via `O_NONBLOCK`); seek with `SEEK_DATA=3` (skip cleared) / `SEEK_END=2`. Detects : (1) **ring-buffer wraparound losing crash context** — compute oldest-seq vs newest-seq vs `log_buf_len` (from `/proc/cmdline` + `/sys/module/printk/parameters/log_buf_len`), surface "kernel ring 256 KiB rolling every 4 min — bump `log_buf=4M` on cmdline" so XID storms don't truncate prior root-cause, (2) **`dmesg_restrict=1` blocking dashboard read** when not root → surface as posture finding "GUI cannot read kernel log — set `dmesg_restrict=0` or run dashboard as user with `CAP_SYSLOG`", (3) **`kptr_restrict=2`** masking pointer addresses in oops traces (makes shipped `xid_decoder.py` output unhelpful), (4) **per-facility/priority histogram** — last-N-minutes counters split by SYSLOG facility (kern=0, user=1, daemon=3, auth=4) and priority (EMERG=0..DEBUG=7), surface "spike of priority=4 warnings from facility=kern in last 5 min", (5) **`printk_ratelimit` drops** — kmsg structured continuation records (`KEY=value`) include `SUBSYSTEM=` and `DEVICE=`; count `SUBSYSTEM=nvme` lines dropped via ratelimit (visible in trailing `[dropped: N]` summary records), (6) **`printk_devkmsg=ratelimit`** — userspace writers (systemd) being throttled into the kernel buffer. First module : `kmsg_audit.py`, GET `/api/kmsg-audit?window=300` returns `{ring_buffer:{size_bytes:262144,oldest_age_s:243,roll_period_estimate_s:243,verdict:"WARN",issue:"ring wraps every ~4 min, XID context will be lost"},policies:{dmesg_restrict:1,kptr_restrict:2,printk_devkmsg:"on",printk_ratelimit:5,printk_ratelimit_burst:10,verdict:"WARN",findings:["dmesg_restrict=1 — non-root dashboard cannot tail kernel"]},histogram:{by_priority:{"0":0,"1":0,"2":0,"3":1,"4":48,"5":12,"6":1241,"7":18},by_facility:{kern:1212,daemon:108}},recent_high_priority:[{ts_us:"...",pri:4,fac:"kern",msg:"nvme0n1: I/O timeout"}],dropped_total:412,verdict_overall:"WARN"}`. Pairs with shipped `journal_audit.py` (post-mortem on-disk) for end-to-end "live ring + archived journal" visibility. |
| 49.2 | **`/sys/class/tpm/tpm*/{device/{description,active_locality,enabled,owned,timeouts,durations,caps,pcr-sha1/*,pcr-sha256/*},tpm_version_major,ppi/{request,response,version}}` + `/sys/kernel/security/tpm0/{binary_bios_measurements,ascii_bios_measurements}` + `/dev/tpmrm0`-presence + IMA-runtime-measurement-list TPM v1.2/2.0 inventory + PCR-state + measured-boot log + IMA-policy auditor — distinct from shipped `security_posture.py` (LSM/seccomp/kernel-lockdown only)** | S | 5 | NO shipped module reads TPM sysfs or the kernel measured-boot log. Most modern motherboards (X670E, Z790, server boards) have a fTPM 2.0 or dTPM 2.0 — invisible to dashboards but the linchpin of measured boot, SecureBoot attestation, LUKS-with-TPM, sbctl signing. Detects : (1) **TPM present but not initialized** — `enabled=0` or `owned=0` means BIOS option is off; surface "fTPM disabled in BIOS, LUKS-with-TPM unavailable", (2) **PCR-state snapshot** — dump PCR0..PCR23 SHA-256 to a single fingerprint; if it changes between boots without a firmware update, surface as a measured-boot drift alarm (Evil Maid detection on the cheap), (3) **`binary_bios_measurements` not exported** by kernel (needs `CONFIG_IMA_MEASURE_PCR_IDX`) → posture finding, (4) **IMA runtime-measurement list size** — `/sys/kernel/security/integrity/ima/runtime_measurements_count` — if 0, IMA is not measuring, surface "no measured-boot chain to attest from", (5) **PPI (Physical Presence Interface) pending op** — `/sys/class/tpm/tpm0/ppi/request` non-zero means an operation (TPM clear, take ownership) is queued for next reboot — *very* useful warning for "why did my LUKS key disappear after reboot?", (6) **TPM `timeouts` / `durations`** — abnormally high values indicate firmware bug throttling TPM ops (signing slow, slowing `systemd-cryptsetup`). First module : `tpm_audit.py`, GET `/api/tpm-audit`. Pairs with shipped `security_posture.py` and shipped `dmi_bios.py` for a full firmware-trust posture. |
| 49.3 | **`/sys/class/wmi/*/{instance_count,expensive,setable,object_id,guid}` + `/sys/bus/wmi/devices/*/{driver,modalias,uevent}` + `/sys/devices/platform/{thinkpad_acpi,asus-wmi,asus-nb-wmi,dell-laptop,dell-smbios,hp-wmi,msi-ec,gigabyte-wmi,framework_laptop}/*` WMI-method + vendor-platform-driver auditor (battery-charge-thresholds, fan-mode, panel-overdrive, RGB-led, dGPU-mux, thermal-table)** | S | 4 | NO shipped module reads WMI / vendor-platform sysfs. WMI (Windows Management Instrumentation on Linux via `acpi-wmi`) exposes hundreds of vendor-specific control methods normally only reached via OEM apps (Armoury Crate, Legion Vantage, Dell Command). Linux drivers (`asus-wmi`, `thinkpad_acpi`, `dell-smbios-wmi`, `hp-wmi`, `gigabyte-wmi`, `msi-ec`, `framework_laptop`) project them to sysfs : battery `charge_control_start_threshold` / `charge_control_end_threshold` (extend battery life for laptop+eGPU rigs), `fan_mode` (override BIOS fan curve), `dgpu_disable` (toggle the discrete GPU on hybrid systems), `panel_overdrive`, `gpu_mux_mode` (MUX-switch a Framework 16 between iGPU-only and dGPU-passthrough), `throttle_thermal_policy` (ASUS thermal profile). Detects : (1) **battery permanently charging to 100 %** on a laptop that hosts a Razer-Core 3090 → "set `charge_control_end_threshold=80` to triple battery cycle life", (2) **WMI method exposed but unused** — list "expensive" WMI methods (those that block firmware) the user might want to query manually, (3) **Vendor fan-mode in `quiet`** mode silently throttling everything (pairs with shipped 47.2 `acpi_audit.py` platform_profile but vendor-specific), (4) **MUX state on Framework / ROG** — surface "GPU MUX = `optimus`, switch to `discrete` for native RTX 3090 attach without Optimus overhead", (5) **RGB / keyboard-backlight stuck-on** wasting 2-3 W idle. First module : `wmi_vendor_audit.py`, GET `/api/wmi-vendor-audit`. Subsumes parked-bench item 33.5 (vendor-platform driver inventory). |
| 49.4 | **`/dev/rtc0` (read-only ioctl `RTC_RD_TIME`, `RTC_WKALM_RD`, `RTC_PIE_*`) + `/sys/class/rtc/rtc*/{name,date,time,since_epoch,hctosys,wakealarm,max_user_freq}` + `/sys/class/pps/pps*/{name,assert,clear,path}` + `/proc/timer_list` + `/sys/devices/system/clocksource/clocksource0/{available_clocksource,unbind_clocksource,current_clocksource}` RTC drift + wakealarm + PPS-source + hrtimer-pending auditor — distinct from shipped `clocksource_audit.py` (global current_clocksource only) and shipped `clock_gap.py` / `clock_offsets.py` (NTP offset)** | XS | 4 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/class/rtc/` or `/dev/rtc0`. Detects : (1) **RTC vs kernel-time skew** — compute `RTC_RD_TIME` − `gettimeofday()`; >2 s drift means CMOS battery dying (very common on year-old motherboards) → "after next power-cut, your box will boot with wrong time, NTP will then have to discipline several hours of drift, kerberos/SSL clients break for minutes", (2) **`wakealarm` set but forgotten** — sysfs `wakealarm` epoch shows the absolute next-wake; if a stale value from a crashed `rtcwake` is still armed, box wakes from sleep at random — surface, (3) **`hctosys=0`** — kernel did not set system time from RTC at boot → surface "you depend entirely on NTP for time, install `systemd-timesyncd` or set `hctosys=1`", (4) **PPS source presence** — most homelabs don't run PPS but if `/sys/class/pps/pps0/` exists, NTP can use it; surface "PPS source `parport-pps` detected but no chrony refclock configured", (5) **`/proc/timer_list` top hrtimers** — surface top 5 pending hrtimers by `softexpires-now` to see which subsystem owns the next wakeup (TuneD, systemd, llama-server's `pthread_cond_timedwait`), (6) **`max_user_freq` too low** — capped at 64 Hz by default, blocks fast PIE clients. First module : `rtc_clock_audit.py`, GET `/api/rtc-clock-audit`. Pairs with shipped `clock_gap.py` / `clock_offsets.py`. |
| 49.5 | **`/sys/kernel/mm/transparent_hugepage/{enabled,defrag,khugepaged/*,shmem_enabled,hpage_pmd_size}` + `/sys/kernel/mm/hugepages/hugepages-*/{nr_hugepages,nr_overcommit_hugepages,free_hugepages,resv_hugepages,surplus_hugepages}` + `/proc/meminfo` (`AnonHugePages`, `ShmemHugePages`, `HugePages_*`) + `/proc/sys/vm/{nr_hugepages,hugetlb_shm_group,nr_overcommit_hugepages}` static-vs-anon hugepage backing + khugepaged-rate + reservation-policy auditor — distinct from shipped `thp_audit.py` (THP `enabled`/`defrag` toggles only) and shipped `vm_sysctl_audit.py` (general /proc/sys/vm)** | S | 3 | Shipped `thp_audit.py` reads only top-level THP toggle; this is the *static-hugetlb + khugepaged* side which it doesn't touch (and we explicitly avoid `/proc/sys/vm/*` for general sysctl per CLAUDE.md, but the *hugepages-specific* nodes are under `/sys/kernel/mm/hugepages/` which is fair game). Static hugepages still matter for inference : CUDA `cudaMallocHost` / `cuMemMap` use locked pages, and reserving 2 MiB hugepages for the kernel slab cache reduces TLB misses on the host-side input/output staging buffers. Detects : (1) **`khugepaged` thrashing** — `pages_collapsed` / `pages_scanned` ratio + `scan_sleep_millisecs` settings; bursty defrag at inference start adds 50-300 ms tail latency, (2) **`nr_hugepages` reserved but unused** — `free_hugepages == nr_hugepages`, surface "256 × 2 MiB reserved but never touched — 512 MiB locked away from page cache", (3) **`hugetlb_shm_group=0`** preventing non-root processes from `shmget(SHM_HUGETLB)` — surface "set `hugetlb_shm_group=<gid>` for llama-server group", (4) **`hpage_pmd_size`** mismatch with kernel build (rare cross-arch issue), (5) **AnonHugePages vs HugePages_Total** ratio — if 99 % of GiB allocations go through THP-anon while user set up `nr_hugepages=512` for inference, the static pool is wasted — surface "static hugepool unused, your workload uses THP-anon". First module : `hugepage_audit.py`, GET `/api/hugepage-audit`. Subsumes parked-bench item 39.6 (khugepaged scan-rate). |
| 49.6 | **`/proc/locks` + `/proc/self/mountinfo` (lockmount discovery) + `/sys/kernel/security/lockdown` + `/proc/keys` (read-only) + `/proc/sys/kernel/{yama/*,kexec_load_disabled,modules_disabled,kptr_restrict,perf_event_paranoid,unprivileged_bpf_disabled}` file-locks + kernel-lockdown-level + Yama-ptrace-policy + perf-paranoid + unprivileged-bpf auditor — distinct from shipped `security_posture.py` (LSM only), shipped `file_locks_audit.py` (just /proc/locks counts), shipped `keyring_audit.py` (just /proc/keys)** | S | 3 | Shipped `file_locks_audit.py` already counts `/proc/locks` entries (so this module focuses on the *security/exposure-policy* superset around it). Detects : (1) **lockdown=`integrity` vs `confidentiality`** — many users don't realize "Secure Boot on" auto-enables lockdown=integrity which blocks `/dev/mem`, `kexec_file_load(unsigned)`, BPF — explains "I can't run my profile tools" → surface, (2) **`yama/ptrace_scope`** > 0 — blocks gdb attach to llama-server for debugging hangs, surface "set 0 temporarily to attach gdb to a stuck inference process", (3) **`perf_event_paranoid` > 1** — blocks `perf stat` from collecting CPU counters without root, surface ; relevant because shipped `cpu_rapl.py` falls back to perf events sometimes, (4) **`unprivileged_bpf_disabled=2`** — Debian 12 default — blocks libbpf-based observability tooling, surface, (5) **`kexec_load_disabled=1`** — surface as posture "rebooting without firmware POST is unavailable", useful for fast iteration on remote boxes, (6) **`modules_disabled=1`** — locks module-loading after boot ; surface so user knows `modprobe nvidia` will fail until reboot, (7) cross-reference with shipped `file_locks_audit.py` for FUSE/NFS lock holders. First module : `kernel_exposure_audit.py`, GET `/api/kernel-exposure-audit`. |
| 49.7 | **`/sys/devices/system/cpu/cpufreq/{boost,policy*/{scaling_governor,scaling_min_freq,scaling_max_freq,scaling_setspeed,energy_performance_preference,energy_performance_available_preferences,bios_limit}}` + `/sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu*/cpufreq/{base_frequency,cpb,scaling_cur_freq,stats/{trans_table,total_trans,time_in_state}}` + `/sys/devices/system/cpu/intel_pstate/{status,no_turbo,hwp_dynamic_boost,max_perf_pct,min_perf_pct}` + `/sys/devices/system/cpu/amd_pstate/{status,prefcore}` per-policy cpufreq + intel/amd_pstate runtime auditor — distinct from shipped `pstate_audit.py` (status-only), `cpu_boost.py` (single boost toggle), `hwp_epp.py` (HWP energy/perf preference only), `cpuidle_audit.py` (cstates not pstates)** | S | 3 | Shipped `pstate_audit.py` reads `intel_pstate/status` and a few top-level toggles; shipped `cpu_boost.py` toggles `boost`; shipped `hwp_epp.py` reads EPP. NONE walks the per-policy tree under `/sys/devices/system/cpu/cpufreq/policy*/` (one dir per cpufreq domain — on AMD hybrid this is per CCX, on Intel hybrid this is P-cluster vs E-cluster) or the per-CPU `cpufreq/stats/` time-in-state histograms. Detects : (1) **per-policy `scaling_max_freq` clipped below `cpuinfo_max_freq`** — user (or TuneD) capped P-core max at 4.8 GHz forgetting they did so 6 months ago, costing 700 MHz on inference, surface, (2) **`bios_limit`** lower than spec — BIOS option "CPU Max Frequency" set by ME/PSP, surface "BIOS clamps your i9-12900K to 5.0 GHz, spec is 5.2 GHz", (3) **`scaling_governor` inconsistent across policies** — P-cluster on `schedutil` but E-cluster on `powersave` → inference unpinned threads silently demoted, (4) **`time_in_state` distribution** — if cpu0 spent 92 % at minimum freq during last hour while inference was supposedly hot, governor is mis-tracking, (5) **`amd_pstate/prefcore`** — AMD preferred-core list (best-bin cores marked for OS-scheduler steering), surface so user can pin llama-server to preferred cores, (6) **`intel_pstate/hwp_dynamic_boost=0`** — disables short-burst HWP boost, hurts decode-spike latency. First module : `cpufreq_policy_audit.py`, GET `/api/cpufreq-policy-audit`. |
| 49.8 | **`/proc/buddyinfo` (already covered) ADJACENT : `/proc/pagetypeinfo` + `/sys/kernel/mm/page_owner/enabled` + `/proc/zoneinfo` (already covered too) — better candidate : `/sys/class/devfreq/*/{governor,available_governors,cur_freq,min_freq,max_freq,target_freq,polling_interval,trans_stat}` + `/sys/class/devlink/*/{auto_remove_on,runtime_pm,sync_state_only,uevent}` devfreq (memory-controller / GPU-power-rail dvfs governors on platforms that expose them) + device-links + suppliers/consumers auditor for understanding which device wakes which** | M | 2 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/class/devfreq/` or `/sys/class/devlink/`. Devfreq is the kernel DVFS framework parallel to cpufreq, governing devices like the IMC, integrated GPU memory controller, DRAM bandwidth scaling on some platforms (Tegra, modern Intel SoCs expose `dmc-freq`), and the GPU on integrated NVIDIA Tegra/jetson but NOT on dGPU RTX 3090 — fit is lower here because most desktop boxes won't have many devfreq nodes. Device-links (`/sys/class/devlink/`) is more universal : every PM-domain dependency is materialized as a devlink (`supplier=0000:00:1d.0`, `consumer=0000:01:00.0`), explains "I unbound the GPU but the box still won't suspend" — some PCIe root-port has `sync_state_only=0` keeping it active. Detects : (1) **devfreq governor on userspace stuck**, (2) **devlink chains preventing runtime PM** — count consumers of GPU's PCIe slot, surface "5 devlinks block d3cold on 0000:01:00.0", (3) **`auto_remove_on=consumer-unbind`** misuse leaving orphan links. Heavier (M) because devlink graph parsing + cross-reference to PCI BDF. First module : `devfreq_devlink_audit.py`. |

### Top 4 picked for cycle #49

**49.1 kmsg_audit** (S) — `/dev/kmsg` + `/proc/sys/kernel/printk*` ring-buffer live-tail + facility/priority histogram + ratelimit-drop + restriction-policy auditor (ring wraparound losing crash context, `dmesg_restrict=1` blocking GUI, `kptr_restrict=2` hiding oops pointers, ratelimit drops on `nvme:` floods)
**49.2 tpm_audit** (S) — `/sys/class/tpm/*` + `/sys/kernel/security/tpm0/binary_bios_measurements` + `/proc/sys/kernel/keys` TPM 1.2/2.0 inventory + PCR-state + measured-boot log + PPI pending-op auditor (fTPM disabled in BIOS, PCR drift between boots, pending PPI clear, IMA not measuring)
**49.3 wmi_vendor_audit** (S) — `/sys/class/wmi/*` + `/sys/devices/platform/{thinkpad_acpi,asus-wmi,dell-smbios,hp-wmi,msi-ec,gigabyte-wmi,framework_laptop}/*` WMI-method + vendor-platform-driver auditor (battery charge thresholds, fan-mode override, dGPU-mux state, vendor thermal profile, RGB stuck-on)
**49.4 rtc_clock_audit** (XS) — `/dev/rtc0` ioctl + `/sys/class/rtc/*` + `/sys/class/pps/*` + `/proc/timer_list` RTC drift + wakealarm + PPS-source + hrtimer-pending auditor (CMOS battery dying, stale wakealarm waking box from sleep, `hctosys=0`, PPS refclock unused)

Bench (49.5 hugepage_audit / 49.6 kernel_exposure_audit / 49.7 cpufreq_policy_audit / 49.8 devfreq_devlink_audit) for cycles after top 4 lands.

---

## R&D #48 survey (started 2026-05-23)

8 fresh angles, none in shipped list (#6-47 — including just-shipped `sched_audit` / `acpi_audit` / `nvidia_rm_audit` / `mce_audit` from cycle #47), modules tree (171 files), or parked bench (27.2/27.5/27.6/27.8 + 28.2/28.3/28.6/28.8 + 29.2/29.4/29.5/29.6 + 30.4/30.6/30.7/30.8 + 31.5/31.6/31.7/31.8 + 32.2/32.6/32.7/32.8 + 33.3/33.5/33.7/33.8 + 34.5/34.6/34.7/34.8 + 35.5/35.6/35.7/35.8 + 36.5/36.6/36.7/36.8 + 37.5/37.6/37.7/37.8 + 38.5/38.6/38.7/38.8 + 39.5/39.6/39.7/39.8 + 40.5/40.6/40.7/40.8 + 41.5/41.6/41.7/41.8 + 42.5/42.6/42.7/42.8 + 43.5/43.6/43.7/43.8 + 44.5/44.6/44.7/44.8 + 45.5/45.6/45.7/45.8 + 46.5/46.6/46.7/46.8 + 47.5/47.6/47.7/47.8). Forbidden / over-covered zones avoided : `/proc/interrupts`, `/proc/softirqs`, `/proc/schedstat`, `/sys/class/thermal`, `/sys/class/net/*`, `/proc/sys/net/*`, `/proc/sys/vm/*`, `/proc/sys/fs/*`, `/sys/firmware/acpi/*`, `/proc/driver/nvidia/*`, `/sys/devices/system/machinecheck`. Stdlib + jsonschema only, single-GPU desktops / homelab focus (RTX 3090 reference), GUI-controllable from Svelte 5 settings.

| # | Feature | Effort | Fit | Why it matters / first module |
|---|---------|--------|-----|-------|
| 48.1 | **`/sys/kernel/tracing/{available_events,set_event,tracing_on,trace_pipe,events/<sys>/<event>/{enable,filter,trigger,hist}}` + `/sys/kernel/debug/tracing/{current_tracer,trace_options,buffer_size_kb}` ftrace event/tracer enablement-state + buffer-size + currently-active-probes auditor — distinct from any shipped module (no module touches tracefs) — this is the *kernel-tracing-state visibility* side: who is currently keeping ftrace ON, which gpu/nvme/cgroup events are being recorded, is `trace_pipe` being drained?** | S | 5 | NO shipped module reads tracefs / debugfs tracing state. When a developer (or rogue script, or stuck `bpftrace` invocation) leaves `tracing_on=1` with `current_tracer=function_graph` and the kernel buffer at 8 MiB per CPU, the box silently burns 5-15 % CPU in ftrace callsites — particularly painful for inference where every `__schedule()` call gets stamped. Visible only here because `top` doesn't show ftrace overhead as a process, and `dmesg` is silent. Detects : (1) **`tracing_on=1` with non-`nop` tracer left over from prior debugging session** — surface "function_graph tracer active for 4h22m on all 32 CPUs — buffer size 8 MiB/CPU = 256 MiB pinned, decode t/s -8 %; remedy `echo 0 > /sys/kernel/tracing/tracing_on`", (2) **enabled events in `set_event`** — list every active event filter (e.g. `sched:sched_switch`, `nvme:nvme_complete_rq`, `drm:drm_vblank_event`) which may have been left enabled by `perf record` / `trace-cmd` that crashed mid-session, (3) **trace_pipe reader missing** — if `trace_pipe` has no consumer but events keep flowing, kernel buffer overruns and drops events silently; surface dropped-event counter via per-CPU `stats` file, (4) **kprobe / uprobe inventory** — walk `/sys/kernel/tracing/{kprobe_events,uprobe_events}` to list dynamic probes still installed; bcc/bpftrace crashes can leave orphan kprobes that fire on every matching kernel function for the box lifetime, (5) **`trace_clock` not `local`** — `global` clock is much slower (cross-CPU TSC sync) and adds 100-300 ns per probe. First module : `ftrace_audit.py`, GET `/api/ftrace-audit` returns `{tracing_on:true,current_tracer:"function_graph",buffer_size_kb_per_cpu:8192,total_pinned_mib:256,active_events:[{event:"sched:sched_switch",enabled:true},{event:"nvme:nvme_complete_rq",enabled:true}],kprobes:[{name:"p_do_sys_open_0",addr:"do_sys_open",enabled:true,verdict:"WARN",issue:"orphan kprobe from prior bpftrace session"}],uprobes:[],trace_pipe_consumer:null,dropped_events_24h:182412,trace_clock:"local",verdict:"WARN",findings:[{level:"WARN",issue:"function_graph tracer active 4h22m — disable via `echo 0 > /sys/kernel/tracing/tracing_on`"}]}`. Pairs naturally with shipped `sched_audit.py` and shipped `irq_rates_audit.py` for end-to-end "is something measuring me right now?" introspection. |
| 48.2 | **`/sys/bus/usb/devices/*/{bConfigurationValue,bMaxPower,bmAttributes,authorized,authorized_default,power/{autosuspend_delay_ms,control,wakeup,active_duration,connected_duration},product,manufacturer,version,speed,bcdDevice,quirks}` USB-tree power-budget + autosuspend-policy + authorized-state + quirks-bitmap auditor for inference rigs with USB-attached UPS/dongles/printers — distinct from any shipped module (no USB module shipped)** | S | 5 | NO shipped module enumerates `/sys/bus/usb/devices/`. USB is the elephant in every inference rig: 4-port USB-C hub for capture cards + the UPS HID + Logitech receiver + Yubikey + Bluetooth dongle + game-controller dongle for OpenWebUI testing... and each device negotiates `bMaxPower` (mA at 5 V). RTX 3090 boxes commonly trip motherboard USB-power-budget when `bMaxPower` total > 1500 mA per controller, causing **random USB device drop-out under sustained inference load** (motherboard VRM thermal throttle drops 5 V rail to 4.7 V, USB devices renumerate, NUT loses UPS comm, inference continues but UPS monitoring goes dark). Detects : (1) **Per-controller power-budget overcommit** — sum `bMaxPower` per `usbN` controller, surface "controller usb2 advertising 6 ports × 500 mA but motherboard hub only 1500 mA — overcommitted by 1500 mA", (2) **`autosuspend_delay_ms=-1`** for HID UPS — Linux defaults autosuspend the USB-HID UPS after 2 s of no traffic, which then reports stale battery state to `power_supply_audit.py` (parked 47.5); surface "hidpp0 autosuspended — battery readings >5 min stale, set `power/control=on`", (3) **`authorized=0` devices** — orphaned devices the user revoked via `udev`, surface, (4) **USB quirks** — `/sys/bus/usb/devices/*/quirks` exposes per-device quirk bitmap (`USB_QUIRK_RESET`, `USB_QUIRK_NO_LPM`, `USB_QUIRK_DELAY_INIT`); if every device on a port has `NO_LPM` set, that controller's link-power-management is disabled (burns 1-2 W extra at idle), (5) **`active_duration / connected_duration` ratio** — `< 0.1` means a USB device is mostly suspended (good), `> 0.95` while idle means stuck-awake firmware bug (Logitech Bolt receivers had this in 2024), (6) **link speed mismatch** — capture card claiming `bcdUSB=0310` but `speed=480` → bad cable / port, surface "EzCAP4K negotiating USB 2.0 only — check cable". First module : `usb_topology_audit.py`, GET `/api/usb-topology-audit` returns `{controllers:[{name:"usb1",speed:"super-speed-plus",devices:6,bmaxpower_total_ma:2200,budget_ma:1500,overcommit_ma:700,verdict:"WARN"}],devices:[{path:"1-1.4",product:"Back-UPS XS 1500U",speed:"full-speed",bmaxpower_ma:100,autosuspend_delay_ms:2000,control:"auto",verdict:"WARN",issue:"HID UPS autosuspending — stale battery readings"},{path:"2-2",product:"EzCAP4K Capture",version:"3.10",speed:"high-speed",verdict:"WARN",issue:"USB 3.x device negotiated USB 2.0 — check cable"}],findings:[{level:"WARN",issue:"controller usb1 power-budget overcommit 700 mA"}],verdict:"WARN"}`. |
| 48.3 | **`/sys/class/dma/dma*chan*/{in_use,device,bytes_transferred}` + `/sys/devices/system/clocksource/clocksource*/{current_clocksource,available_clocksource,unbind_clocksource,available_clocksource_per_cpu}` + `/sys/devices/pci*/*/iommu_group/devices/*` + `/sys/class/swiotlb/{bytes_used,nr_used,nr_slots}` DMA-engine channel + SWIOTLB-bounce-buffer usage + clocksource-per-CPU audit — distinct from shipped `clocksource_audit.py` (global current_clocksource only) and shipped `iommu_groups.py` (only group enumeration) — this is the *DMA-engine + SWIOTLB-pressure + per-CPU-clocksource* side: is the box bouncing every GPU DMA through SWIOTLB because IOMMU passthrough broke, are some CPUs on a different clocksource?** | S | 4 | Shipped `clocksource_audit.py` reads the *global* `current_clocksource` from `/sys/devices/system/clocksource/clocksource0/` only; many kernels expose per-CPU clocksource state under `clocksource1..clocksourceN` when the user has `nohz_full=` partitioning isolating some CPUs to a different timer. NO module touches `/sys/class/dma/` or SWIOTLB stats. Detects : (1) **SWIOTLB bounce-buffer saturation** — when `iommu=pt` is missing and the GPU does H2D over PCIe with addresses above 4 GiB, kernel routes through SWIOTLB; default 64 MiB buffer fills under sustained training/inference (10 GiB/s through a 64 MiB ring = wraparound every 6.4 ms, contention spikes), surface "SWIOTLB 92 % full, 4214 slots used / 4 K — set `swiotlb=131072` on cmdline OR enable `iommu=pt`", (2) **DMA-engine `in_use=1` on ioat / dw_dmac channels** — if any IOAT channel is in-use during inference, some out-of-tree driver is leeching DMA copy capacity from system memory bandwidth, (3) **per-CPU clocksource divergence** — if CPU0-7 use `tsc` but CPU8-15 use `hpet` (because the user passed `clocksource=hpet` on a `nohz_full=8-15` cmdline by accident), inter-CPU timestamp comparisons in llama-server (mutex tracing) become non-monotonic, surface, (4) **dma_chan parented to wrong PCI device** — if `dma0chan0/device` points to the GPU instead of system DMA engine, custom kmod is hijacking GPU DMA. First module : `dma_audit.py`, GET `/api/dma-audit`. |
| 48.4 | **`/var/log/journal/<machine-id>/*.journal` + `/run/log/journal/<machine-id>/*.journal` via stdlib `struct` parser (journal binary format documented in `systemd-journal-binary-format(7)`) + `/etc/systemd/journald.conf{,.d/*}` parsing for journal-disk-budget + rate-limit + ForwardToSyslog + per-priority counters auditor for last-24h ERR/CRIT/EMERG entries** | M | 4 | NO shipped module reads journal binary or `journald.conf`. Stdlib-only journal-binary parsing is non-trivial but doable: header magic `LPKSHHRH`, 256-byte header, then chained Object entries (Data, Field, Entry, DataHash, FieldHash, EntryArray, Tag) with offsets and a streamable layout. Many distros default `Storage=auto` which means **journal is volatile** in `/run` and lost on reboot — losing the only record of "what XID error fired before kernel panic". `SystemMaxUse=`, `RuntimeMaxUse=`, `MaxFileSec=`, `RateLimitIntervalSec=`, `RateLimitBurst=` control disk-budget and rate-limiting; `RateLimitBurst=1000` drops kernel `nvrm:` messages during XID storms — losing crash root-cause attribution. Detects : (1) **journal volatile** — `/var/log/journal/` missing or empty → "journal is RAM-only, you will lose all XID/oops logs on reboot; `mkdir /var/log/journal && systemctl restart systemd-journald`", (2) **rate-limit drops** — count `__REALTIME_TIMESTAMP` gaps + cross-reference with `journalctl --verify` Dropped counts, surface "12 K messages dropped in last 24 h — bump RateLimitBurst to 10000", (3) **SystemMaxUse exhaustion** — if `du /var/log/journal == SystemMaxUse`, old XID context being aged out, surface, (4) **kernel ERR/CRIT/EMERG histogram for last 24 h** without shelling out to `journalctl` (which is not stdlib) — gives offline post-mortem capability when `journalctl` itself fails to start (corruption), (5) **`ForwardToSyslog=yes`** while no rsyslog/syslog-ng installed → write amplification with no observability gain. Subsumes parked-bench item 42.6 (journal-disk-budget). First module : `journal_audit.py`, GET `/api/journal-audit`. Heavier (M) because binary format parsing needs offset chasing + checksum validation. |
| 48.5 | **`/sys/class/pwm/pwmchip*/{npwm,export,pwm*/{period,duty_cycle,enable,polarity}}` + `/sys/class/leds/*/{brightness,max_brightness,trigger}` + `/sys/class/backlight/*/{brightness,max_brightness,actual_brightness,bl_power}` PWM-output + LED-state + backlight inventory auditor for case-fan PWM headers, RGB-strip kernel control, OLED-panel HDR-burn risk** | XS | 3 | NO shipped module reads PWM/LED/backlight. Many AIO water-cooled RTX 3090 rigs route case-fan PWM through motherboard-PWM headers exposed at `/sys/class/pwm/pwmchip0/pwm0/` — and the kernel's `pwm-aspeed` / `pwm-stm32` drivers will let you write `duty_cycle` directly. Detects : (1) **PWM-controlled case fans pegged to 0** — when shipped `fan_curve.py` lowered GPU fan to silent profile during idle, but a custom udev rule pegged case-fan PWM to 0, GPU memory heatsoaks, (2) **kernel LED-trigger inventory** — list which `nvme0-led` / `disk-led` / `bluetooth-led` triggers are firing; useful for "my SSD activity LED is blinking even when nothing should be touching the disk", (3) **OLED backlight kept at max** for 24/7 dashboard mode → HDR burn-in risk for users running coreprose / OpenWebUI fullscreen on OLED, surface "backlight intel_backlight 100 % for 18h — risk", (4) **backlight `actual_brightness ≠ brightness`** — firmware overriding software set, common on hybrid-graphics ThinkPads. First module : `pwm_led_audit.py`, GET `/api/pwm-led-audit`. |
| 48.6 | **`/sys/class/hwmon/hwmon*/{name,in*_input,in*_label,curr*_input,curr*_label,power*_input,power*_label,energy*_input}` + `/sys/class/regulator/regulator.*/{name,microvolts,microamps,opmode,state}` voltage-rail + current-draw + regulator-state full inventory (beyond temp/fan) — distinct from shipped `hwmon_inventory.py` (which focuses on `temp*` + `fan*` discovery) and shipped `cpu_rapl.py` (RAPL package-level only) — this is the *voltage / current / regulator* side: is the VRM 12 V rail sagging under inference load, is the SoC SVI3 reporting per-core current spikes, is a regulator stuck in eco-mode?** | S | 3 | Shipped `hwmon_inventory.py` lists chips and temp/fan endpoints but doesn't drill into `in*` (voltage), `curr*` (current), `power*` non-RAPL inputs. Many modern motherboards (X670E, Z790) expose nct6798d/it8688 hwmon nodes with `in0`=Vcore, `in1`=12V, `in2`=AVCC, `in3`=3.3V, `curr1`=EPS-12V current, `power1`=total CPU power; on AMD AM5, `k10temp` companion `zenpower3` exposes SVI3 per-die voltage/current. Detects : (1) **12 V rail sagging below 11.4 V** under sustained inference — undersized PSU or daisy-chained EPS cables, surface "EPS12V dropped to 11.32 V at GPU stress peak — PSU undersized for sustained 350 W GPU + 200 W CPU", (2) **Vcore lockstep with VID** — diff Vcore against MSR-reported VID (via shipped `cpu_rapl.py` adjacency) — divergence means BIOS LLC misconfig, (3) **regulator stuck in eco** — some laptop dGPU regulators expose `state=disabled` or `opmode=idle` after a failed suspend — explains "GPU only gets 80 W now, why?", (4) **inference power-attribution split** — sum hwmon `power*` to validate against UPS-reported wall power (shipped `wall_meter.py`); divergence >15 % → measurement chain broken. First module : `voltage_current_audit.py`, GET `/api/voltage-current-audit`. |
| 48.7 | **`/sys/class/nvmem/*/nvmem` + `/sys/bus/nvmem/devices/*/{name,type,size}` + `/sys/class/spi_master/spi*/{name,bus_num}` + `/sys/bus/spi/devices/*/{modalias,driver}` NVMEM (one-time-programmable / SPI-EEPROM / fuses) + SPI-flash inventory + BIOS-region read auditor — distinct from shipped `dmi_bios.py` (DMI/SMBIOS user-facing tables only) and shipped `vbios_drift.py` (GPU VBIOS) — this is the *non-volatile motherboard storage* side: what fuses, what EEPROM, what BIOS-image SPI-flash chip?** | M | 2 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/class/nvmem/` (kernel NVMEM framework — fuses, OTP, board EEPROM, RTC NVRAM). Useful for : (1) **board EEPROM fingerprint** — many motherboards expose serial / batch / MAC in `at24` EEPROM at `/sys/class/nvmem/0-00500/nvmem` (read-only, can be hashed for inventory), (2) **CPU-fuse decoding** — Intel exposes some fuse state via NVMEM (turbo-bin, AVX-512 disabled flag); useful for "my i9 has AVX-512 disabled at fuse level — surface this so user knows llama.cpp `avx512` build won't help", (3) **SPI BIOS-flash detection** — `/sys/class/spi_master/spi0/` + child `/sys/bus/spi/devices/0.0/modalias=spi:w25q256` reveals BIOS chip part-number, useful for safe flashing workflows, (4) **RTC NVRAM contents** for boards exposing it via `/sys/class/nvmem/rtc0/nvmem`. Lower fit because most homelab users don't tune fuses, but the inventory is unique. First module : `nvmem_spi_audit.py`. |
| 48.8 | **`/sys/class/extcon/extcon*/{name,state,uevent}` + `/sys/class/typec/*/{port_type,power_role,data_role,vconn_source,supported_accessory_modes,active_pdo}` + `/sys/class/usb_role/*/role` USB-C / USB-PD power-delivery + DisplayPort-alt-mode + role-swap state auditor for laptops with USB-C-attached eGPU (RTX 3090 in Razer Core enclosure) and USB-C displays** | M | 2 | NO shipped module reads extcon / typec / usb_role. Critical for laptop+eGPU inference rigs (less common but growing — Framework 16 + Razer Core X with 3090 inside). Detects : (1) **USB-C PD-negotiation degraded** — `active_pdo` shows current Power Delivery contract (e.g. `15V@3A=45W` instead of expected `20V@5A=100W`) → eGPU underpowered, GPU silently throttling to 200 W max, (2) **typec port stuck in `data_role=device`** when it should be `host` after dock-swap, (3) **DP-alt-mode not engaged** — `supported_accessory_modes` shows DP but `active_pdo` doesn't include DP — external monitor sees host GPU iGPU not eGPU dGPU, (4) **extcon disconnect events** — count Thunderbolt link-drops per hour. Lower fit because RTX 3090 reference is desktop not laptop+eGPU, but USB-C displays are mainstream now. First module : `usbc_pd_audit.py`. |

### Top 4 picked for cycle #48

**48.1 ftrace_audit** (S) — `/sys/kernel/tracing/*` + `/sys/kernel/debug/tracing/*` ftrace state + buffer + active-events + orphan-kprobes auditor (left-over function_graph tracer eating CPU, orphan kprobes from crashed bpftrace, trace_pipe drop-counter)
**48.2 usb_topology_audit** (S) — `/sys/bus/usb/devices/*/{bMaxPower,power/*,authorized,quirks,speed,bcdDevice}` USB tree power-budget + autosuspend + speed-negotiation auditor (USB controller power-budget overcommit causing UPS drop-outs, HID-UPS autosuspended reporting stale battery, USB 3.x device renegotiated to 2.0)
**48.3 dma_audit** (S) — `/sys/class/dma/*` + `/sys/class/swiotlb/*` + per-CPU clocksource DMA-engine + SWIOTLB-bounce + per-CPU-clocksource auditor (SWIOTLB saturation when `iommu=pt` missing, IOAT DMA hijack, nohz_full per-CPU clocksource divergence)
**48.4 journal_audit** (M) — `/var/log/journal/*` binary parser + `/etc/systemd/journald.conf*` + rate-limit-drop + priority-histogram auditor (volatile-journal losing XID logs, RateLimitBurst dropping nvrm messages, SystemMaxUse aging out crash context)

Bench (48.5 pwm_led_audit / 48.6 voltage_current_audit / 48.7 nvmem_spi_audit / 48.8 usbc_pd_audit) for cycles after top 4 lands.

---

## R&D #47 survey (started 2026-05-23)

8 fresh angles, none in shipped list (#6-46 — including just-shipped `softirq_audit` / `security_posture` / `vfs_limits_audit` / `keyring_audit` from cycle #46), modules tree (167 files), or parked bench (27.2/27.5/27.6/27.8 + 28.2/28.3/28.6/28.8 + 29.2/29.4/29.5/29.6 + 30.4/30.6/30.7/30.8 + 31.5/31.6/31.7/31.8 + 32.2/32.6/32.7/32.8 + 33.3/33.5/33.7/33.8 + 34.5/34.6/34.7/34.8 + 35.5/35.6/35.7/35.8 + 36.5/36.6/36.7/36.8 + 37.5/37.6/37.7/37.8 + 38.5/38.6/38.7/38.8 + 39.5/39.6/39.7/39.8 + 40.5/40.6/40.7/40.8 + 41.5/41.6/41.7/41.8 + 42.5/42.6/42.7/42.8 + 43.5/43.6/43.7/43.8 + 44.5/44.6/44.7/44.8 + 45.5/45.6/45.7/45.8 + 46.5/46.6/46.7/46.8). Forbidden / over-covered zones avoided : `/proc/interrupts`, `/proc/softirqs`, `/sys/class/thermal`, `/sys/class/net/*`, `/proc/sys/net/*`, `/proc/sys/vm/*`, `/proc/sys/fs/*`. Stdlib + jsonschema only, single-GPU desktops / homelab focus (RTX 3090 reference), GUI-controllable from Svelte 5 settings.

| # | Feature | Effort | Fit | Why it matters / first module |
|---|---------|--------|-----|-------|
| 47.1 | **`/proc/schedstat` + `/proc/sched_debug` + `/sys/kernel/debug/sched/{features,latency_ns,migration_cost_ns,min_granularity_ns,wakeup_granularity_ns,tunable_scaling}` CPU-scheduler runqueue-latency + wakeup-cost + migration-count + sched-feature auditor — distinct from shipped `proc_sched.py` (per-task `/proc/<pid>/sched` snapshot), shipped `psi_pressure.py` (PSI summary), shipped `smt_audit.py` (SMT topology) — this is the *CFS/EEVDF runqueue-internals* side: how long are inference threads waiting in the runqueue, how often are they being migrated cross-NUMA, are SCHED_FEAT flags hostile to single-GPU latency?** | S | 5 | NO shipped module reads `/proc/schedstat` or `/proc/sched_debug`. `schedstat` format : header `version 15` + `timestamp <jiffies>` then per-CPU lines `cpu<N> <yld_count> <sched_count> <sched_goidle> <ttwu_count> <ttwu_local> <rq_cpu_time> <run_delay> <pcount>` where `run_delay` is cumulative ns spent waiting on runqueue and `pcount` is task switches — deltas reveal **per-CPU runqueue-wait pressure** with attribution. `/proc/sched_debug` dumps per-runqueue stats including `nr_running`, `nr_uninterruptible`, `next_balance`, `curr->pid`, `runnable_avg`, `util_avg`, plus per-cfs_rq weight/load tree — the *only* stdlib way to see EEVDF lag without bpftrace. Auditor detects : (1) **runqueue-wait pile-up on isolated CPUs** — when llama-server is pinned to CPU 8-15 via cgroup but the host runs Plex+Docker on CPU 0-7, the inference threads accumulate `run_delay` deltas of 200-800 µs per scheduling slice (visible as inter-token jitter); without this module the user sees "p99 inter-token latency 35 ms vs p50 18 ms" and blames the model when it's actually CFS load-balancer pulling the thread off CPU8 every 4 ms because some Electron renderer briefly spiked CPU8, (2) **excessive cross-NUMA migrations** — `sched_debug` exposes `nr_migrations` per-task and per-CPU; on dual-socket workstations or hybrid Alder/Raptor Lake (P/E-core boundary acts like NUMA), inference threads bouncing P→E mid-decode lose all L2/L3 cache warmth; surface migration rate per cgroup, (3) **SCHED_FEAT mis-config** — `/sys/kernel/debug/sched/features` lists ~30 toggles (`GENTLE_FAIR_SLEEPERS`, `NEXT_BUDDY`, `LAST_BUDDY`, `WAKEUP_PREEMPTION`, `UTIL_EST`, `UTIL_EST_FASTUP`, `TTWU_QUEUE`, `LB_BIAS`, ...); kernel-tuning guides on Reddit recommend disabling `GENTLE_FAIR_SLEEPERS` for "lower latency gaming" — but the same tweak destroys inference throughput by letting interactive tasks preempt llama-server's decode loop; surface drift from kernel-build defaults, (4) **`latency_ns` / `min_granularity_ns` / `wakeup_granularity_ns` debugfs tunables** — TuneD `latency-performance` profile sets `min_granularity_ns=10000000` which keeps llama-server's `pthread_cond_wait()` blocked an extra 10 ms before reschedule; for token-decode workloads `1000000` (1 ms) is optimal but no GUI surface today, (5) **per-CPU `idle_balance` cost** — `sched_debug` shows `idle_balance` time; a domain-balance loop that takes 4-8 ms on each CPU0 wakeup explains "Bluetooth keystroke latency went up after I bought a 7960X". First module : `sched_audit.py`, GET `/api/sched-audit?window=10` returns `{schedstat:{per_cpu:[{cpu:0,run_delay_us_per_s:412,task_switches_per_s:5821,verdict:"OK"},{cpu:8,run_delay_us_per_s:8120,task_switches_per_s:12821,verdict:"WARN",issue:"llama-server runqueue-wait p99 ≈ 8 ms — preempted by cross-cgroup tasks"}],imbalance_ratio:19.7,verdict:"WARN"},features:{GENTLE_FAIR_SLEEPERS:true,NEXT_BUDDY:false,WAKEUP_PREEMPTION:true,drift_from_default:[]},debugfs_tunables:{latency_ns:24000000,min_granularity_ns:3000000,wakeup_granularity_ns:4000000,migration_cost_ns:500000,verdict:"WARN",issue:"min_granularity_ns=3ms — inference threads see +3ms wakeup tail; set 1ms for decode latency"},sched_debug:{nr_running_top:[{cpu:0,nr:5},{cpu:8,nr:3}],nr_uninterruptible:2,top_migrators:[{pid:48211,comm:"llama-server",migrations_per_s:42,verdict:"WARN"}]},verdict_overall:"WARN"}`. Pairs with shipped `numa_placement.py` and `proc_sched.py` for end-to-end "task-pinning intent → actual runqueue-wait" auditing. |
| 47.2 | **`/sys/firmware/acpi/platform_profile{,_choices}` + `/proc/acpi/wakeup` + `/sys/firmware/acpi/{bgrt,fpdt,interrupts/*}` + `/sys/devices/LNXSYSTM:00/.../wakeup/*` ACPI platform-profile + GPE wakeup-source rate + spurious-wake-attribution + BGRT/FPDT boot-timing auditor — distinct from shipped `suspend_guard.py` (gates inference-time suspend via `/proc/acpi/button/lid/`) — this is the *ACPI-stack control surface* side: what platform-profile is the firmware in, which GPE is firing at 8 kHz wasting CPU, which `/proc/acpi/wakeup` device should be disabled?** | S | 5 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/firmware/acpi/*` or `/proc/acpi/wakeup` (suspend_guard touches only `/proc/acpi/button/lid/`). `platform_profile` is a one-line writable file (`low-power`, `balanced`, `balanced-performance`, `performance`, `cool`, `quiet`) shipped by Lenovo Legion / ASUS ROG / Dell Precision firmware — switches CPU/GPU TDP envelopes and fan-curve presets *behind the OS's back*. Many users don't know it exists and run RTX 3090 workstation BIOS at `quiet` losing 15-25 % sustained throughput. `/proc/acpi/wakeup` lists every ACPI-named device with its wakeup-enable status (`*disabled` / `*enabled`) — common spurious wake culprits : `XHCI` (USB), `RP05`/`RP09` (PCIe root-port for the GPU itself, which then wakes the GPU from D3cold and burns 30 W idle), `GLAN` (onboard NIC with WoL). `/sys/firmware/acpi/interrupts/gpe*` exposes per-GPE counters — runaway GPE (firing 1000-10000 times/s) usually means a broken DSDT method retriggering itself, visible only here. `/sys/firmware/acpi/bgrt/{image,status,type,version,xoffset,yoffset}` and `/sys/firmware/acpi/fpdt/boot/*` expose boot-time milestones (`firmware_start_ns`, `bootloader_launch_ns`, `exitbootservices_start_ns`, `exitbootservices_end_ns`) — useful for "my box takes 28 s to POST after I added the RTX 3090" → BIOS option-ROM resource-shuffle visible in FPDT delta. Detects : (1) **`platform_profile=quiet` on a workstation** — surface in dashboard with one-click switch to `balanced-performance`, (2) **GPE storm** — any GPE with `count` delta >100/s in 10 s window → flag with DSDT-grep hint, (3) **PCIe root-port wakeup-enabled** preventing GPU D3cold (pairs with shipped `d3cold_policy.py`), (4) **`XHCI` wakeup-enabled with USB-attached UPS/HID** waking box every minute, (5) **slow EFI handover** via FPDT — if `exitbootservices_end − firmware_start > 10 s`, GPU option-ROM is being initialized twice (CSM-compat residue). First module : `acpi_audit.py`, GET `/api/acpi-audit` returns `{platform_profile:{current:"quiet",choices:["low-power","balanced","balanced-performance","performance"],verdict:"WARN",remedy:"echo balanced-performance > /sys/firmware/acpi/platform_profile"},wakeup_devices:[{name:"XHCI",status:"enabled",bus:"pci",sysfs:"PNP0D10"},{name:"RP05",status:"enabled",verdict:"WARN",issue:"PCIe root-port wakeup blocking GPU D3cold"},{name:"GLAN",status:"enabled"}],gpe_top:[{gpe:"gpe6E",count_total:12842,count_per_s:0.4,verdict:"OK"},{gpe:"gpe17",count_per_s:184.2,verdict:"WARN",issue:"GPE storm — broken DSDT method?"}],fpdt_boot_timing_ms:{firmware_start:0,exitbootservices_end:4820,total_firmware_ms:4820,verdict:"OK"},bgrt_present:true,verdict_overall:"WARN"}`. Subsumes parked-bench item 41.7 (platform-profile drift) with broader scope. |
| 47.3 | **`/proc/driver/nvidia/params` + `/proc/driver/nvidia/registry` + `/proc/driver/nvidia/version` + `/proc/driver/nvidia/capabilities/{mig,gpu*/mig,nvlink*}` nvidia RM-runtime registry-key + capability inventory auditor — distinct from shipped `kmod_params.py` (which reads `/sys/module/nvidia/parameters/`, modprobe-time config) and shipped `proc_deep_state.py` (which reads `/proc/driver/nvidia/gpus/<bdf>/information` per-GPU dynamic state) — this is the *RM-internal live registry + cgroup-capability fd* side: what runtime RegistryDwords are active, what nvidia-capabilities does my cgroup actually allow access to?** | XS | 5 | NO shipped module reads `/proc/driver/nvidia/params`, `registry`, or the `capabilities/` tree. `/proc/driver/nvidia/params` is fundamentally different from `/sys/module/nvidia/parameters/`: the sysfs surface shows *modprobe* time params (`NVreg_*`), while `/proc/driver/nvidia/params` shows the *running RM registry* including dynamically-applied `NVreg_RegistryDwords` like `RMNvLinkBandwidthLinkCount=0x0,RMIntrLockingMode=0x2,RMDevSemPollAllowedDelay=0x3e8` — values that may have been silently downgraded by RM at runtime if the GPU rejected them. `/proc/driver/nvidia/registry` lists every active `<key,type,value,flags>` tuple — vital for "my benchmark.sh sets `NVreg_RestrictProfilingToAdminUsers=0` but nsight still refuses, why?" (answer : driver compiled with profiling-locked-out at build time, visible only in registry). `/proc/driver/nvidia/capabilities/` is the kernel-cgroup capability tree (`mig-config`, `mig-monitor`, per-GPU `nvlink/*`) — each capability is a 0-byte file whose presence is gated by `nvidia-modprobe -c 0 -u`; if a container has bind-mounted `/proc/driver/nvidia/capabilities/` but missed a subdir, MIG/NVLink ops fail with cryptic `NVML_ERROR_INSUFFICIENT_PERMISSIONS`. Auditor detects : (1) **registry value silently downgraded** — diff `/sys/module/nvidia/parameters/NVreg_RegistryDwords` (requested) vs `/proc/driver/nvidia/registry` (active), surface keys where requested != active, (2) **capability dir missing under containerized inference** — common cause of MIG fails inside `nvidia-container-toolkit` rootless setups, (3) **`/proc/driver/nvidia/version` driver string drift** vs `nvidia-smi --query-gpu=driver_version` (mismatch on partial DKMS rebuild after kernel upgrade — a known footgun where userspace is 555.x but kmod is 550.x → CUDA inits fail at API mismatch), (4) **`Mode=` field in params indicating RM persistence-mode state** independent of `nvidia-persistenced.service`. First module : `nvidia_rm_audit.py`, GET `/api/nvidia-rm-audit` returns `{driver_version_proc:"555.42.06",driver_version_smi:"555.42.06",version_match:true,registry_keys:[{key:"RMNvLinkBandwidthLinkCount",value:"0x0",requested:"0x0",match:true},{key:"RMIntrLockingMode",value:"0x2",match:true},{key:"NVreg_RestrictProfilingToAdminUsers",value:"0",effective:"locked-by-build",verdict:"WARN",issue:"requested 0 but RM ignores — rebuild with --tools-profiler"}],capabilities:{mig_config_present:false,mig_monitor_present:false,nvlink_present:false,per_gpu:[{bdf:"0000:01:00.0",caps:["mig"],missing:[]}],verdict:"OK"},params_mode:"Mode=0 (false)",verdict_overall:"WARN"}`. |
| 47.4 | **`/sys/devices/system/machinecheck/machinecheck*/{check_interval,cmci_disabled,ignore_ce,monarch_timeout,tolerant,trigger,bank*}` + `/dev/mcelog` (read-only header) + `/sys/devices/system/edac/mc/mc*/{ce_count,ue_count,seconds_since_reset}` MCE bank-tunable + CMCI-state + recent-MCE-count auditor — distinct from shipped `edac_ram_ecc.py` (DIMM-level CE/UE counts via EDAC's row/column attribution) — this is the *MCE-machinery-layer* side: are CMCI interrupts disabled, what are the per-bank thresholds, is `tolerant` set so high we silently swallow uncorrectable errors?** | S | 4 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/devices/system/machinecheck/`. Format : one dir per logical CPU (`machinecheck0..machinecheckN`) with same-attribute mirroring; key files : `check_interval` (poll seconds, default 300), `cmci_disabled` (0/1 — Corrected-Machine-Check-Interrupt vs polling), `ignore_ce` (0/1 — silently drop CE), `monarch_timeout` (µs — MCE-monarch sync window), `tolerant` (0/1/2/3 — 0=panic on UE, 3=ignore everything), and per-bank `bank0..bank31` mask (writable for selective disable, often abused to silence noisy memory banks instead of replacing DIMMs). Detects : (1) **`ignore_ce=1` masking real RAM errors** — some Dell PowerEdge BIOSes set this from firmware to "improve uptime metrics"; the dashboard's shipped `edac_ram_ecc.py` then shows zero CE because kernel never sees them; surface with critical verdict, (2) **`tolerant=3` swallowing UE** — homelab user copy-pasted from a Reddit "stop the kernel panicking" thread, now silently corrupting RAM during inference, (3) **`cmci_disabled=1` on AMD EPYC** — known interaction with AMD CMCI errata, but for Intel desktops should be 0 — if 1, CE go undetected for up to 300 s, (4) **`check_interval` lowered to 1** — burns CPU on MCE polling 300x more, visible perf hit, (5) **per-bank mask** — if `bank4` (typically DRAM channel) is masked, surface in posture report. First module : `mce_audit.py`, GET `/api/mce-audit` returns `{cpus:32,uniform:true,check_interval_s:300,cmci_disabled:false,ignore_ce:false,tolerant:1,monarch_timeout_us:1000000,bank_masks:[{bank:0,mask:"0x1"},{bank:4,mask:"0x0",verdict:"OK"}],recent_mce_24h:0,findings:[],verdict:"OK"}`. Pairs naturally with shipped `edac_ram_ecc.py` and `retired_pages.py` for full "what does the kernel actually see vs what's being silenced" memory-fault posture. |
| 47.5 | **`/sys/class/power_supply/*/{type,status,online,capacity,voltage_now,current_now,energy_now,energy_full,charge_now,model_name,manufacturer,scope,usb_type}` kernel-native power-supply auditor for USB-HID UPS + laptop battery + AC-online state machine — distinct from shipped `ups_nut.py` (NUT-daemon protocol via TCP socket) and shipped `ups_runtime.py` (runtime estimation via NUT) — this is the *kernel sysfs power-supply class* side: works when `nut-server` is not installed, reads the UPS the same way `upower` does, and adds laptop-BAT support for laptop GPU rigs.** | XS | 4 | NO shipped module reads `/sys/class/power_supply/`. Every USB-HID-class UPS (APC Back-UPS, CyberPower CP1500, EATON Ellipse PRO that supports USB-HID-PD) shows up as `/sys/class/power_supply/hidppX/` via the `hid-input` driver — *zero NUT daemon required*. Laptop batteries appear as `BAT0`/`BAT1`; AC adapter as `AC`/`ACAD`/`AC0`. Reads cost <1 ms (vs ~50 ms for NUT TCP roundtrip when nut-server runs on a remote pi). Auditor detects : (1) **USB-HID UPS detected but NUT not configured** — surface "found `Back-UPS XS 1500U` at `/sys/class/power_supply/hidpp0/` with 78 % battery, 230 V mains, on-line — no nut.conf detected, dashboard can read directly via sysfs", (2) **AC offline + battery <20 %** — emit critical alert for laptop dGPU rigs running inference where shutdown is imminent, (3) **`capacity_level=Critical`** with `status=Discharging` even though sysfs `online=1` — UPS misreporting; surface mismatch, (4) **laptop BAT `energy_full / energy_full_design < 0.6`** — battery health <60 %, surface "consider not relying on this BAT for inference burst budget", (5) **`scope=System` UPS reporting `current_now=0` for >5 min while host load >100 W** — UPS shunt failed, runtime estimate from shipped `ups_runtime.py` invalid; surface mismatch. First module : `power_supply_audit.py`, GET `/api/power-supply-audit` returns `{supplies:[{name:"hidpp0",type:"UPS",status:"Discharging",online:false,capacity_pct:78,voltage_v:230.1,model:"Back-UPS XS 1500U",manufacturer:"American Power Conversion",scope:"System",verdict:"WARN",issue:"AC offline — running on UPS, 78% battery"},{name:"BAT0",type:"Battery",status:"Full",capacity_pct:100,energy_full_wh:48.2,energy_full_design_wh:56.0,health_pct:86,verdict:"OK"},{name:"AC",type:"Mains",online:false,verdict:"WARN"}],ac_present:false,ups_present:true,verdict_overall:"WARN"}`. Subsumes parked-bench item 37.5 (USB-HID UPS direct read). |
| 47.6 | **`/sys/bus/pci/slots/*/{address,cur_bus_speed,max_bus_speed,power}` + `/sys/bus/pci/devices/*/{enable,broken_parity_status,subsystem_device,subsystem_vendor,resource,d3hot_delay,d3cold_delay,reset_method,current_link_speed,max_link_speed,msi_bus,revision}` + `/sys/bus/pci/drivers/*/{module,uevent}` PCI-slot + driver-binding + per-device resource-map inventory — distinct from shipped `pcie_*` modules (link-state / AER / ASPM / width / histogram), `msi_inventory.py` (MSI vector counts), and `gpu_pci_bind.py` (single bind/unbind action) — this is the *static topology + driver-binding lineage* side: which physical slot is the GPU in, which slots are empty but powered, which devices have no driver bound at all?** | S | 3 | NO shipped module enumerates `/sys/bus/pci/slots/` or per-device `enable`/`broken_parity_status`/`reset_method`. Detects : (1) **GPU in slot below 16x physical** — `/sys/bus/pci/slots/0/address` says GPU is in slot whose `max_bus_speed=8.0 GT/s` not `16.0 GT/s` — physical x8 slot wired as x16, surface "your RTX 3090 is in a slot mechanically/electrically x8 — verify chassis silkscreen", (2) **Orphan PCI devices with no driver** — walk `/sys/bus/pci/devices/*/driver` symlink (missing for unbound), surface "0000:04:00.0 (`Realtek RTL8125 NIC`) has no driver bound — `modprobe r8169`", (3) **`reset_method`** — shows whether device supports `flr`/`af_flr`/`pm`/`bus`/`device_specific` reset; useful when `gpu_reset.py` fails — surface "this GPU reports `reset_method=bus` only — full bus reset will reset adjacent devices in same slot", (4) **`d3hot_delay_ms` excessive** — some buggy GPU firmwares advertise 100 ms d3hot delay, surface, (5) **empty hotplug slot still drawing power** via `/sys/bus/pci/slots/*/power` write-back, useful for under-desk noise hunting. First module : `pci_topology_audit.py`, GET `/api/pci-topology-audit`. |
| 47.7 | **`/proc/mtrr` + `/sys/firmware/memmap/*/{start,end,type}` + `/sys/kernel/mm/page_idle/bitmap`-presence + `/sys/devices/system/memory/{block_size_bytes,memory*/{online,state,removable}}` MTRR region-map + E820 firmware-memory-map + memory-hotplug-block + page-idle-tracker auditor for write-combining BAR1 / PMR / CMP regions correctness** | S | 3 | NO shipped module reads `/proc/mtrr`, `/sys/firmware/memmap/`, or `/sys/devices/system/memory/`. `/proc/mtrr` (Intel MTRR registers, slowly being replaced by PAT but still authoritative on many BIOSes) describes write-combining (WC) regions — critical because GPU BAR1 (the framebuffer-mapped portion CUDA uses for D2H/H2D over PCIe) *must* be marked WC for full PCIe-write-throughput; if the BIOS programmed a stale UC range over the GPU BAR (after a hot-swap, or because IOMMU shuffled things), H2D bandwidth drops 4-8x silently. `/sys/firmware/memmap/*/` exposes the parsed E820 map (`Reserved`, `System RAM`, `ACPI Tables`, `BIOS-e820 type=20`, `unusable`) — invaluable for "I bought 128 GB but kernel only sees 96 GB" (firmware reserved 32 GB above the 64-bit-MMIO hole for the GPU CMP region). `/sys/devices/system/memory/memory*/online` reveals memory-hotplug blocks taken offline — sometimes by mistake via udev rule. Detects : (1) **GPU BAR1 not WC** — cross-reference `/sys/bus/pci/devices/0000:01:00.0/resource` with `/proc/mtrr` WC ranges; if BAR1 region not covered by any WC entry, surface critical alert with `setpci`/`modprobe` remedy, (2) **E820 reserved hole eating RAM** — if `firmware_reserved_bytes > 1 GiB`, surface "BIOS reserved X GiB above MMIO hole — see Above 4G Decoding / Re-Size BAR setting", (3) **memory block offlined** — `memory42/online=0` after fault recovery, RAM unavailable, (4) **`page_idle/bitmap` presence** — surface as a capability flag for future memory-coldness module. First module : `mtrr_memmap_audit.py`, GET `/api/mtrr-memmap-audit`. |
| 47.8 | **`/sys/class/iommu/*/devices/` + `/sys/kernel/iommu_groups/*/{reserved_regions,type}` + `/sys/class/iommu/dmar*/{intel-iommu/{cap,ecap,version,address}}` or `/sys/class/iommu/ivhd*/amd-iommu/{cap,features}` IOMMU runtime-state + reserved-region + capability auditor — distinct from shipped `iommu_groups.py` (which only enumerates groups + flags `passthrough_safety`) — this is the *IOMMU-hardware-capability + reserved-region-tracking* side: does my IOMMU support nested paging for upcoming SR-IOV, what DMA regions did firmware reserve that my kernel can't touch?** | M | 2 | Shipped `iommu_groups.py` only walks `/sys/kernel/iommu_groups/*/devices/`. Detects : (1) **`reserved_regions`** — each group's `reserved_regions` file lists DMA holes (`direct`, `direct-relaxable`, `msi`) — a misconfigured reserved region (e.g., IGFX-stolen RAM at low memory) can break GPU-direct RDMA setups, (2) **Intel VT-d `ecap`** missing `Nested Translation Support` — surface "your IOMMU does not support nested paging — upcoming SR-IOV for vGPU won't work", (3) **AMD IOMMUv2 features** — `IOMMU_FEATURE_GT` for PASID/PRI required by upcoming HMM-on-AMD support, (4) **`type` per-group** (`DMA`, `DMA-FQ`, `identity`, `auto`) — surface drift from kernel cmdline `iommu=pt`. Heavier (M) because per-arch parsing (Intel cap bitfield is 64-bit packed, AMD different). First module : `iommu_caps_audit.py`. |

### Top 4 picked for cycle #47

**47.1 sched_audit** (S) — `/proc/schedstat` + `/proc/sched_debug` + `/sys/kernel/debug/sched/*` CFS/EEVDF runqueue-wait + migration-cost + sched-feature auditor (runqueue pile-up on isolated CPUs, cross-NUMA migrations, hostile SCHED_FEAT flags)
**47.2 acpi_audit** (S) — `/sys/firmware/acpi/platform_profile` + `/proc/acpi/wakeup` + `/sys/firmware/acpi/{interrupts,fpdt,bgrt}` ACPI platform-profile + GPE storm + spurious-wakeup auditor (workstation stuck in `quiet` profile, GPE storms, PCIe root-port wakeup blocking GPU D3cold)
**47.3 nvidia_rm_audit** (XS) — `/proc/driver/nvidia/{params,registry,version,capabilities/}` nvidia RM-runtime registry-key + cgroup-capability auditor (silently-downgraded RegistryDwords, missing capability dirs in containers, DKMS userspace/kmod version drift)
**47.4 mce_audit** (S) — `/sys/devices/system/machinecheck/machinecheck*/*` MCE bank-tunable + CMCI-state + recent-MCE auditor (`ignore_ce=1` silencing CE, `tolerant=3` swallowing UE, masked DRAM-channel banks)

Bench (47.5 power_supply_audit / 47.6 pci_topology_audit / 47.7 mtrr_memmap_audit / 47.8 iommu_caps_audit) for cycles after top 4 lands.

## R&D #46 survey (started 2026-05-23)

8 fresh angles, none in shipped list (#6-45 — including just-shipped `nf_conntrack_audit` / `mdraid_health` / `sysvipc_audit` / `entropy_audit` from cycle #45), modules tree (164 files), or parked bench (27.2/27.5/27.6/27.8 + 28.2/28.3/28.6/28.8 + 29.2/29.4/29.5/29.6 + 30.4/30.6/30.7/30.8 + 31.5/31.6/31.7/31.8 + 32.2/32.6/32.7/32.8 + 33.3/33.5/33.7/33.8 + 34.5/34.6/34.7/34.8 + 35.5/35.6/35.7/35.8 + 36.5/36.6/36.7/36.8 + 37.5/37.6/37.7/37.8 + 38.5/38.6/38.7/38.8 + 39.5/39.6/39.7/39.8 + 40.5/40.6/40.7/40.8 + 41.5/41.6/41.7/41.8 + 42.5/42.6/42.7/42.8 + 43.5/43.6/43.7/43.8 + 44.5/44.6/44.7/44.8 + 45.5/45.6/45.7/45.8). Stdlib + jsonschema only, single-GPU desktops / homelab focus (RTX 3090 reference), GUI-controllable from Svelte 5 settings.

| # | Feature | Effort | Fit | Why it matters / first module |
|---|---------|--------|-----|-------|
| 46.1 | **`/proc/softirqs` + `/proc/stat` softirq-line-per-CPU per-vector deltas (HI / TIMER / NET_TX / NET_RX / BLOCK / IRQ_POLL / TASKLET / SCHED / HRTIMER / RCU) softirq-pressure + per-CPU saturation auditor — distinct from shipped `irq_rates_audit.py` (which reads `/proc/interrupts` — hardware IRQ side), shipped `gpu_irq_affinity.py` (steering knob), and shipped `nic_queue_affinity.py` (NIC RPS/XPS side) — this is the *softirq-context bottom-half* side: where is `ksoftirqd/N` burning CPU, is NET_RX softirq starving NET_TX, is RCU softirq backlogged?** | S | 5 | NO shipped module reads `/proc/softirqs`. Format : header line of CPU columns + one line per softirq vector with per-CPU cumulative counter (`HI`, `TIMER`, `NET_TX`, `NET_RX`, `BLOCK`, `IRQ_POLL`, `TASKLET`, `SCHED`, `HRTIMER`, `RCU`). Sampling deltas at 1 s intervals over 30-60 s reveals: (1) **NET_RX softirq pinned to CPU0 starving inference threads** — when NIC has no `RPS`/`XPS` configured, all RX softirq lands on CPU0; under sustained 1 Gbps llama-server SSE fan-out (10 clients × 80 tok/s × 6 KB chunks), CPU0 spends 60-90 % in softirq context, preempting any inference thread the scheduler tries to put there; the symptom is "decode t/s drops 15-25 % whenever a second OpenWebUI client connects" but `top` shows `si` only on CPU0 and most users don't know `si%` is softirq; surface "NET_RX softirq 78 % on CPU0 (others <2 %) — bump `/sys/class/net/eth0/queues/rx-0/rps_cpus`", (2) **RCU softirq backlog** — `RCU` softirq counter spiking on every CPU simultaneously indicates kernel RCU-callback queue depth exceeded `rcu_blimit`; correlate with `dmesg | grep "rcu_sched detected stall"`; surface "RCU softirq +18 K in 5 s — possible RCU stall, check kernel build CONFIG_RCU_BOOST", (3) **TIMER softirq saturation from runaway hrtimer** — if HRTIMER+TIMER softirq sum >5 K/s on a single CPU while shipped `clocksource_audit.py` shows TSC stable, indicates a userspace process arming hrtimers at sub-ms cadence (Discord client polling every 100 µs, broken Electron app), (4) **BLOCK softirq pinned to wrong CPU vs NVMe IRQ affinity** — combined with shipped `irq_rates_audit.py` reveals "NVMe IRQ on CPU2, but BLOCK softirq drains on CPU0 → cross-CPU cache miss every I/O completion", (5) **TASKLET dead** — TASKLET softirq should be near-zero on modern kernels; if growing >100/s, an out-of-tree kmod is using legacy tasklet API and may have a deadlock bug. First module : `softirq_audit.py`, GET `/api/softirq-audit?window=30` returns `{vectors:{NET_RX:{total_per_s:8421,per_cpu:[8200,42,18,...],dominant_cpu:0,imbalance_pct:97.3,verdict:"WARN",issue:"NET_RX pinned to CPU0 — set rps_cpus"},TIMER:{total_per_s:2412,per_cpu:[400,420,...],verdict:"OK"},RCU:{total_per_s:182,verdict:"OK"},SCHED:{total_per_s:642,verdict:"OK"},HRTIMER:{total_per_s:18,verdict:"OK"},BLOCK:{total_per_s:142,dominant_cpu:0,verdict:"WARN",issue:"BLOCK on CPU0 but nvme0n1 IRQ on CPU2 — cross-CPU completion"},TASKLET:{total_per_s:0,verdict:"OK"},HI:{total_per_s:0,verdict:"OK"},IRQ_POLL:{total_per_s:0,verdict:"OK"},NET_TX:{total_per_s:42,verdict:"OK"}},ksoftirqd_top_cpu_pct:{cpu0:48.2,cpu2:1.1},verdict_overall:"WARN"}`. Pairs naturally with shipped `irq_rates_audit.py` for end-to-end "hardware-IRQ → softirq → inference-thread" latency-budget ribbon. |
| 46.2 | **`/sys/kernel/security/{lockdown,lsm}` + `/proc/sys/kernel/{kptr_restrict,dmesg_restrict,unprivileged_userns_clone,unprivileged_bpf_disabled,yama/ptrace_scope,perf_event_paranoid}` + `/sys/module/apparmor/parameters/{enabled,mode}` + `/sys/fs/selinux/{enforce,policyvers}` host security-posture + LSM-stack inventory auditor — single source of truth for "can I attach a profiler / debugger to llama-server, can BPF read GPU IRQ latency, is the kernel in integrity-locked mode that breaks nvidia.ko reload?"** | S | 5 | NO shipped module reads any LSM state. Today shipped `kernel_taint.py` reads taint bits and shipped `kmod_params.py` reads module params, but neither answers "what *security mode* is this kernel running in and what does it block?". Format : `/sys/kernel/security/lockdown` reads as one line listing modes with the active one in brackets (`none [integrity] confidentiality`), `/sys/kernel/security/lsm` reads as comma-separated LSM stack (`capability,yama,apparmor,bpf`), `/proc/sys/kernel/perf_event_paranoid` is an integer 0-3 (0 = unrestricted, 2 = default Ubuntu, 3 = Debian-hardened), `/proc/sys/kernel/yama/ptrace_scope` is 0-3 (1 = restricted ptrace, common default), `/proc/sys/kernel/unprivileged_userns_clone` (0 = Docker-rootless breaks) + `unprivileged_bpf_disabled` (1 = bcc/bpftrace require root). Auditor detects: (1) **lockdown=integrity blocking nvidia.ko `modprobe`** — when Secure Boot is on, kernel lockdown=integrity refuses to load unsigned out-of-tree modules including DKMS-built `nvidia.ko`; user sees `modprobe: ERROR: could not insert 'nvidia': Operation not permitted` and `dmesg` shows `Lockdown: nvidia: unsigned module loading is restricted; see man kernel_lockdown.7`; surface "lockdown=integrity active — sign nvidia.ko with MOK or disable Secure Boot", (2) **perf_event_paranoid=3 blocking nvidia-nsight / py-spy** — Debian 12 defaults to 3, blocking unprivileged `perf_event_open()`; py-spy + nsight + bpftrace silently fail with `EACCES`; surface "perf_event_paranoid=3 — set to 1 in /etc/sysctl.d/ to enable nvidia-nsight + py-spy without sudo", (3) **yama.ptrace_scope=1 blocking `strace -p <llama-server-pid>` for non-parent user** — common Ubuntu default; user can't debug their own running llama-server; surface, (4) **AppArmor confining nvidia-persistenced** — Ubuntu 24.04 ships `/etc/apparmor.d/usr.bin.nvidia-persistenced` which can DENY `/dev/nvidia-uvm-tools` access on certain CUDA Toolkit versions; surface profile load state, (5) **unprivileged_userns_clone=0 breaks Podman/Docker-rootless** — RHEL/Rocky default; surface, (6) **unprivileged_bpf_disabled=1 + perf_event_paranoid=3 combo** blocks all eBPF observability the dashboard might want to ship later. Subsumes parked bench #38.7 (perf_event_paranoid profiling-readiness) with broader scope. First module : `security_posture.py`, GET `/api/security-posture` returns `{lockdown_mode:"integrity",lsm_stack:["capability","yama","apparmor","bpf"],kptr_restrict:1,dmesg_restrict:1,perf_event_paranoid:2,ptrace_scope:1,unprivileged_userns_clone:1,unprivileged_bpf_disabled:0,apparmor:{enabled:true,mode:"enforce",profiles_loaded:42,nvidia_profiles:["usr.bin.nvidia-persistenced"]},selinux:{enforce:null,policyvers:null},findings:[{level:"WARN",issue:"perf_event_paranoid=2 — py-spy/nsight require sudo; set =1 for inference profiling",remedy:"echo 'kernel.perf_event_paranoid=1' >/etc/sysctl.d/99-gpudash.conf"},{level:"INFO",issue:"lockdown=integrity active — nvidia.ko must be MOK-signed"}],verdict:"WARN"}`. |
| 46.3 | **`/proc/sys/fs/{file-max,file-nr,nr_open,inotify/{max_user_watches,max_user_instances,max_queued_events},epoll/max_user_watches,pipe-max-size,pipe-user-pages-{hard,soft},aio-max-nr,aio-nr,mqueue/{queues_max,msg_max,msgsize_max}}` + `/proc/sys/kernel/pid_max` VFS-global resource-limit + headroom auditor — distinct from shipped `limits_audit.py` (per-process rlimit/ulimit side), shipped `inotify_audit.py` (which is per-user watch *usage*, not global ceilings), and shipped `rlimit_audit.py` — this is the *kernel-wide ceiling* side: how close is the box to global file-max wall, are AIO contexts exhausted, is pid_max about to wrap?** | S | 4 | NO shipped module reads global VFS ceilings. Shipped `limits_audit.py` and `rlimit_audit.py` read per-process `RLIMIT_NOFILE`-style limits; shipped `inotify_audit.py` reads per-user inotify usage — but kernel-global ceilings (the wall behind those limits) live in `/proc/sys/fs/*` and `/proc/sys/kernel/pid_max`. Format : each is a small text file with 1-3 space-separated integers. `file-nr` returns 3 ints (`allocated free max`); `aio-nr` + `aio-max-nr` show kernel AIO context headroom; `pipe-user-pages-{hard,soft}` cap per-user pipe-buffer memory. Auditor detects: (1) **`file-nr` allocated approaching `file-max`** — homelab Jupyter + ollama + browser combo can pin 800 K open FDs (`lsof | wc -l` style aggregate); when `allocated > 80 % of max`, the next `open()` returns `ENFILE` and applications crash with cryptic errors; surface time-to-wall projection at current FD-allocation rate, (2) **`aio-nr` saturation breaking io_uring-based llama-server** — modern llama-server with `--use-uring` allocates kernel AIO contexts; default `aio-max-nr=65536`, each io_uring instance burns up to 1024 entries; 65 simultaneous io_uring contexts wedge new submissions; surface "aio-nr 60 % full — bump aio-max-nr to 262144", (3) **`inotify/max_user_watches` global ceiling vs per-user usage** — shipped `inotify_audit.py` reads usage but never compares to global ceiling on a multi-user box, (4) **`pid_max` headroom** — default `pid_max=4194304` on 64-bit but on legacy 32-bit-tasks kernels (or `kernel.pid_max` lowered for compat) the user can wrap PIDs; surface current `nr_threads` from `/proc/loadavg` field 4 vs ceiling, (5) **`pipe-max-size` too low for large vllm/llama log piping** — default 1 MiB; cargo-cult lowering to 64 KiB breaks `--logging-pipe` workflows. First module : `vfs_limits_audit.py`, GET `/api/vfs-limits-audit` returns `{file_nr:{allocated:82342,free:1024,max:262144,utilization_pct:31.4,verdict:"OK"},aio:{nr:1024,max:65536,utilization_pct:1.6,verdict:"OK"},inotify:{max_user_watches:524288,max_user_instances:128,max_queued_events:16384,verdict:"OK"},epoll:{max_user_watches:524288,verdict:"OK"},pipe:{max_size:1048576,user_pages_hard:0,user_pages_soft:0,verdict:"OK"},pid_max:4194304,nr_threads_now:892,pid_max_utilization_pct:0.02,verdict_overall:"OK"}`. |
| 46.4 | **`/proc/keys` + `/proc/key-users` + `/proc/sys/kernel/keys/{maxbytes,maxkeys,root_maxbytes,root_maxkeys,gc_delay,persistent_keyring_expiry}` kernel-keyring inventory + per-user-keyring quota auditor for ecryptfs / fscrypt / kerberos / DNS-resolver stale-key leaks** | XS | 4 | NO shipped module reads kernel keyring state. Kernel keyrings (`man 7 keyrings`) hold credentials for ecryptfs home-encryption, fscrypt (`/var/lib/ollama` per-user encryption), NFSv4 idmap, Kerberos tickets, DNS resolver caching, ID-mapped mounts (containers), and `keyctl session ...` user sessions. Each user has a quota (`maxbytes`/`maxkeys`); when exceeded, ecryptfs mount fails with `EDQUOT`, NFS idmap stops resolving UIDs and shows numeric UIDs in `ls -l`, Kerberos kinit silently fails. Format : `/proc/keys` is one line per key with `<id> <flags> <usage> <expire> <uid> <gid> <type> <description>: <payload-summary>` (only readable for keys you have View permission on, but readable as root); `/proc/key-users` is one line per UID with `<uid>: <usage>/<nkeys> nkeys=<n> nikeys=<n> qnkeys=<n>/<max> qnbytes=<bytes>/<max>`. Auditor detects: (1) **runaway `.dns_resolver` keys** — long-running llama-server with HF mirror probing creates one `dns_resolver` key per hostname; default expiry 5 min but if `dns_resolver.gc_delay` was bumped for some workaround, keys accumulate; surface key-count time series, (2) **stale Kerberos tickets after ticket-renewal failure** — `krbtgt/REALM@REALM` keys orphaned with expired ts, (3) **fscrypt key-quota approaching** — if user encrypted `~/.cache/huggingface` with fscrypt v2 and accumulated 200 K dentry-key entries, quota hits; surface, (4) **container ID-mapped mount keys leaking from Podman-rootless** — each `podman run --userns=auto` creates an idmapped-mount key that survives container exit due to kmod bug on 6.1-6.5 kernels. First module : `keyring_audit.py`, GET `/api/keyring-audit` returns `{users:[{uid:1000,name:"olivier",nkeys:42,nbytes:8192,quota_keys:200,quota_bytes:20000,utilization_keys_pct:21,utilization_bytes_pct:40,verdict:"OK"},{uid:0,name:"root",nkeys:128,verdict:"OK"}],totals:{keys:182,bytes:38421},top_types:[{type:".dns_resolver",count:48},{type:"user",count:32},{type:"logon",count:12},{type:"big_key",count:1}],findings:[],verdict:"OK"}`. |
| 46.5 | **`/sys/power/{state,disk,mem_sleep,sync_on_suspend,wakeup_count,pm_async,pm_freeze_timeout,pm_test,pm_print_times,pm_wakeup_irq,resume_offset}` + `/sys/kernel/debug/wakeup_sources` + `/sys/power/suspend_stats/{success,fail,failed_freeze,failed_prepare,failed_suspend,last_failed_dev,last_failed_errno,last_failed_step}` suspend/resume-readiness + wakeup-source attribution auditor — distinct from shipped `suspend_guard.py` (which gates inference-time suspend) — this is the *post-mortem + readiness* side: which device blocked the last suspend, what wakeup source brought the box back, is auto-suspend healthy?** | S | 4 | Shipped `suspend_guard.py` prevents suspend during inference but never reports *why a previous suspend failed* or *what woke the box*. `/sys/power/suspend_stats/` aggregates success/fail counters and pinpoints the offending driver (`last_failed_dev=0000:01:00.0` → nvidia GPU, very common cause of failed-suspend on RTX 3090); `/sys/kernel/debug/wakeup_sources` lists every kernel device wakeup-source with `active_count`, `event_count`, `wakeup_count`, `expire_count`, `total_time`, `prevent_suspend_time` — invaluable for "my desktop wakes up from suspend every 3 min for no reason" (usually a USB wireless mouse with bad firmware or NIC with `wol=g` triggered by broadcast traffic). Auditor detects: (1) **last failed suspend due to nvidia.ko** — `last_failed_dev=0000:01:00.0` + `last_failed_errno=-22` → check `/etc/systemd/system/nvidia-suspend.service` is enabled and `nvidia.NVreg_PreserveVideoMemoryAllocations=1` is set, (2) **spurious-wakeup-source leaderboard** — top-N wakeup-sources by `wakeup_count/uptime_h`; flag any USB device with >5 wakes/hour, (3) **`mem_sleep` not set to `deep`** — modern laptops/SFFs default to `s2idle` which can fail on RTX 3090 hybrid-graphics setups; surface, (4) **`sync_on_suspend=0`** — risky for `/var/lib/ollama` mid-`ollama pull` interrupted by lid-close; surface. First module : `suspend_audit.py`, GET `/api/suspend-audit`. |
| 46.6 | **`/sys/kernel/livepatch/*/{enabled,transition,signature,force}` + per-patch `/sys/kernel/livepatch/<name>/<obj>/<func>/{patched,nop,prev}` kernel livepatch + kpatch / Ubuntu Livepatch / Oracle Ksplice inventory auditor** | XS | 3 | NO shipped module reads livepatch state. Format : one subdir per loaded livepatch under `/sys/kernel/livepatch/`. Detects: (1) **kpatch loaded but in `transition` state** for >24 h — means some kthread is permanently stuck in old-function context, blocking patch finalization; CVE remains partially mitigated, (2) **Ubuntu Livepatch service active** but no patches loaded (kernel up-to-date OR canonical-livepatchd broken) — surface diff between `livepatch status` and reality, (3) **livepatch'd nvidia-related symbols** — useful for "why does my nvidia.ko crash only on kernels with livepatch X applied?" debugging. Lower fit because most homelab users don't run livepatch but worth surfacing when present. First module : `livepatch_audit.py`, GET `/api/livepatch-audit`. |
| 46.7 | **`/sys/firmware/efi/efivars/{Boot*-*,BootOrder-*,BootCurrent-*,SetupMode-*,SecureBoot-*,LoaderInfo-*,LoaderDevicePartUUID-*}` + `/sys/firmware/efi/{fw_platform_size,fw_vendor,runtime,config_table}` UEFI variable + boot-order + Secure Boot posture auditor** | M | 3 | NO shipped module reads efivars. Format : each `efivars` entry is a 4-byte attribute header + raw GUID-typed payload; `Boot####` entries follow EFI_LOAD_OPTION (`Attributes(4) | FilePathListLength(2) | Description(wchar*) | FilePathList(...) | OptionalData(...)`); `BootOrder` is a u16 array of boot-entry IDs. Detects: (1) **Secure Boot enabled while nvidia.ko unsigned** (overlaps with 46.2 lockdown but from firmware side, can correlate), (2) **boot-order drift** — Linux Boot#### no longer first after a Windows dual-boot update, (3) **stale `Boot0001` entries** pointing to removed USB media, (4) **`LoaderInfo` from systemd-boot vs grub auto-detection**. Heavier because efivars parsing requires UCS-2 string decoding + EFI_DEVICE_PATH parsing. First module : `efivars_audit.py`. |
| 46.8 | **`/sys/class/scsi_host/host*/{ahci_*,em_*,sas_*,em_message,em_message_supported,em_buffer,unique_id,host_busy,can_queue,cmd_per_lun,supported_mode,active_mode,proc_name,link_power_management_policy}` + `/sys/class/ata_port/ata*/{idle_irq,nr_pmp_links}` SATA/SAS controller + AHCI + enclosure-management + link-PM auditor for boxes with SATA SSDs on PCH** | M | 2 | NO shipped module reads scsi_host. Diagnoses AHCI Link Power Management mis-config (`med_power_with_dipm` saving 1-2 W idle but adding 50-200 ms wake latency on every cold SATA read — invisible in benchmarks because page-cache hides it but visible in `ollama pull` first-touch reads), AHCI `host_busy` queue-depth saturation, enclosure-management LED control for SATA hotswap homelab boxes. Lower fit because RTX 3090 reference rig is typically NVMe-primary (covered by `nvme_iosched.py`), but homelab boxes with 4-8 SATA SSDs in `/var/lib/ollama` benefit. First module : `scsi_host_audit.py`. |

### Top 4 picked for cycle #46

**46.1 softirq_audit** (S) — `/proc/softirqs` + `/proc/stat` per-vector per-CPU softirq saturation auditor (NET_RX pinned to CPU0 starving inference, RCU backlog, BLOCK cross-CPU completion misalignment)
**46.2 security_posture** (S) — `/sys/kernel/security/{lockdown,lsm}` + `/proc/sys/kernel/{perf_event_paranoid,ptrace_scope,unprivileged_*}` + AppArmor/SELinux LSM stack + posture auditor (Secure Boot blocking nvidia.ko, perf_event_paranoid=3 blocking py-spy/nsight)
**46.3 vfs_limits_audit** (S) — `/proc/sys/fs/{file-max,file-nr,aio-max-nr,pipe-max-size,inotify/*,epoll/*}` + `/proc/sys/kernel/pid_max` kernel-global VFS ceiling + headroom auditor (file-nr wall projection, aio-nr breaking io_uring llama-server)
**46.4 keyring_audit** (XS) — `/proc/keys` + `/proc/key-users` + `/proc/sys/kernel/keys/*` kernel keyring inventory + per-user-quota auditor (dns_resolver runaway, ecryptfs/fscrypt quota exhaustion, idmapped-mount key leak)

Bench (46.5 suspend_audit / 46.6 livepatch_audit / 46.7 efivars_audit / 46.8 scsi_host_audit) for cycles after top 4 lands.
