| # | Feature | Effort | Fit | Why it matters / first module |
|---|---------|--------|-----|-------|
| 41.1 | **`/sys/module/zswap/parameters/{enabled,compressor,zpool,max_pool_percent,accept_threshold_percent,same_filled_pages_enabled,non_same_filled_pages_enabled}` + `/sys/kernel/debug/zswap/*` + `/sys/block/zram*/{disksize,comp_algorithm,max_comp_streams,mm_stat,io_stat,bd_stat}` + `/proc/swaps` zswap / zram compressed-swap auditor for 32-GB-host + 70B-quant rigs** | S | 5 | When a homelab user pushes a 70B-quant (~40 GB on disk) onto a 32-GB-RAM host, the *first* swap-pageout latency cliff hits inference t/s the moment context window grows past ~3K tokens — and the kernel offers *two* different compressed-swap layers (zswap = pool-of-LRU-compressed-pages in front of a real backing swap device, zram = pure RAM-backed compressed block device with no disk backing) that together can absorb 60-80 % of swap traffic with single-digit-ms compression latency instead of NVMe's 200-2000 µs read latency. Shipped `nvme_swap.py` watches *whether* NVMe swap is active + SMART endurance; shipped angle 40.3 `vm_tuning_deep.py` covers `page-cluster` + `watermark_scale_factor` + reclaim aggressiveness — but neither walks the zswap+zram compressed-swap layer at all. The recurring foot-guns the audit catches: (1) `zswap.enabled=N` (kernel default on most distros) + 24 GB quant loaded → every page-out hits NVMe directly, ~40-200× slower than enabling zswap with lz4 compressor, (2) `zswap.enabled=Y` but `zswap.compressor=lzo` (legacy default on older kernels) + Zen4/Zen5 host → lz4 is 2-3× faster *and* has better ratio on tensor-blob data, recommend `lz4` or `zstd` with paste-ready snippet, (3) `zswap.max_pool_percent=20` (default) on a 32-GB box loading a 24-GB quant → zswap pool capped at ~6.4 GB, fills instantly under context-growth pressure, recommend `40-50` to give the inference workload a real compression buffer, (4) `zswap.zpool=zbud` (oldest, 2-pages-per-zpool, ~50 % ratio) vs `z3fold` (3-pages, ~67 %) vs `zsmalloc` (best ratio, ~3-4×, default since 6.6) — older kernels default to `zbud`, miss the 2× ratio improvement, (5) zram active *and* zswap active simultaneously with both pointing at the same backing → double-compression latency + wasted CPU, flag the conflict, (6) zram swap configured (`/dev/zram0` in `/proc/swaps`) but `comp_algorithm=lzo-rle` while CPU has hardware-accelerated `lz4` or `zstd` via shipped #cpu_microcode → suboptimal compression-speed/ratio, (7) `same_filled_pages_enabled=Y` (default) catches all-zero pages cheaply — but `non_same_filled_pages_enabled=N` (rare misconfiguration from old `/etc/sysctl.d/`) disables the actual compression path, the user has zswap enabled but it's a no-op, surface clearly. Read all `/sys/module/zswap/parameters/*` (boolean Y/N + string + int), `/sys/kernel/debug/zswap/{pool_total_size,stored_pages,pool_limit_hit,reject_compress_fail,reject_compress_poor,reject_kmemcache_fail,reject_alloc_fail,reject_reclaim_fail,duplicate_entry,written_back_pages,same_filled_pages,zpool_total_size}` (requires `mount -t debugfs none /sys/kernel/debug` — surface availability), walk `/sys/block/zram*/{disksize,initstate,comp_algorithm,max_comp_streams,mem_used_total,mem_used_max,mem_limit,backing_dev,writeback_limit_enable}` + `/sys/block/zram*/mm_stat` (orig_data_size, compr_data_size, mem_used_total, mem_limit, mem_used_max, same_pages, pages_compacted, huge_pages, huge_pages_since), cross-correlate with `/proc/swaps` (which devices are active swap, priority order), shipped #nvme_swap.py (NVMe-side swap presence), shipped #buddyinfo_frag (page fragmentation impacts zpool allocator), shipped #host_class (Proxmox guest can't always read zswap params), classify into 5 verdicts: (a) `zswap.enabled=Y` + `compressor=lz4` or `zstd` + `zpool=zsmalloc` + `max_pool_percent ≥ 30` + active NVMe swap-back → optimal, congratulate + show live compression ratio from debugfs `stored_pages / pool_total_size`, (b) `zswap.enabled=N` + 70B-quant pattern detected (mmap'd file ≥ 20 GB in shipped #service_discovery's inference PID) → recommend enable with paste-ready `/etc/default/grub` `GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT="… zswap.enabled=1 zswap.compressor=lz4 zswap.zpool=zsmalloc zswap.max_pool_percent=40"` snippet + `update-grub` (zswap params are cmdline-time, not runtime), (c) `zswap.enabled=Y` but `compressor=lzo` or `zpool=zbud` → migration recipe, (d) zram swap + zswap both active and overlapping → conflict, recommend zram-only (lower latency, no NVMe wear) for boxes with no real NVMe swap, (e) `same_filled_pages_enabled=N` (misconfigured) → flag, paste-ready re-enable. Surface "your 32-GB host has 24 GB GGUF loaded, `zswap.enabled=N`, 8 GB NVMe swap active with 412 MB swapped → enable zswap with lz4 + zsmalloc + max_pool=40 % to absorb ~60-80 % of swap traffic in-RAM (compression ratio ~2.5-3.0× on quant tensor blobs), cuts swap-in latency from ~1.5 ms to ~50 µs, frees up ~5-6 GB effective addressable RAM" + paste-ready GRUB snippet. Pairs naturally with shipped `nvme_swap.py` (the backing layer), shipped #vm_tuning_deep (page-cluster + watermark), shipped #buddyinfo_frag (allocator fragmentation), shipped #service_discovery (which PID has the giant mmap). The single highest-leverage feature for the RAM-tight + VRAM-rich audience (the dominant homelab pattern for single-RTX-3090 owners pushing 70B-quants) that today nothing in the OSS Linux ecosystem surfaces cleanly. First : `modules/zswap_zram_audit.py` + GET `/api/zswap-zram-audit`. |
| 41.2 | **`/sys/devices/system/edac/mc/mc*/{ce_count,ue_count,size_mb,seconds_since_reset}` + `/sys/devices/system/edac/mc/mc*/csrow*/{ch*_ce_count,ch*_dimm_label,size_mb,edac_mode,mem_type}` + `/sys/devices/system/edac/mc/mc*/dimm*/{dimm_label,dimm_location,size,dimm_dev_type,dimm_edac_mode,dimm_mem_type}` system-RAM ECC error-counter + DIMM-label auditor (sibling to shipped GPU-VRAM `ecc_remap.py`)** | XS | 5 | Shipped `ecc_remap.py` watches *GPU VRAM* ECC events on RTX 3090 (uncorrectable retired pages, single-bit volatile counter, double-bit retirement queue) — but says nothing about *system RAM* ECC, which is the single highest-leverage silent-corruption surface on a homelab inference rig: a single uncorrected DRAM bit-flip in the page where llama-server is dequantising tensor row #471 means the model silently emits a slightly-wrong logit and the user blames "GGUF quantization noise" while actually their cheap non-ECC DDR5 has a marginal IC. The Linux EDAC (Error Detection And Correction) subsystem at `/sys/devices/system/edac/mc/mc*/` is *always present* when the memory controller driver loaded (`amd64_edac` on Zen, `i10nm_edac`/`skx_edac`/`pnd2_edac`/`igen6_edac` on Intel, `armada_xp_edac` on ARM) — but the user has to know to look. The recurring foot-guns the audit catches: (1) `mc/` directory absent entirely → EDAC driver not loaded (`modprobe amd64_edac` would surface ECC capability) — common on minimal Arch installs and on every Ubuntu install on a non-ECC consumer board (the driver loads but mc/ is empty because no ECC channels), surface "your motherboard does NOT have ECC, every silent bit-flip will hit your inference workload and cannot be detected by software", (2) `mc/` present + `ce_count > 0` and incrementing → correctable errors actively happening, your DIMMs are degrading + the next UE may be hours away, paste-ready "swap DIMM in slot $(cat dimm0/dimm_location)" recipe with the DIMM label EDAC exposes (e.g. `DIMM_A1`), (3) `mc/` present + `ue_count > 0` historically → an uncorrectable error happened at some point this boot, the kernel may have silently SIGBUS'd a process (check shipped #nvrm_tail / `dmesg` for MCE events), (4) `mc/` present with `mc_name=ghes_edac` rather than the chipset-specific driver → ACPI/GHES fallback mode, lower-resolution reporting (no per-DIMM labels), recommend installing the chipset driver, (5) ECC capable hardware (`edac_mode != SECDED` despite `ECC` in DMI) → ECC physically present but kernel sees it as non-ECC (BIOS option `ECC=disabled` for stability), surface as "you paid for ECC RAM but BIOS has it disabled, re-enable in `Advanced → Memory → ECC Configuration`", (6) Threadripper Pro / EPYC + ECC working + `ce_count` per `csrow` non-uniform (one csrow has 100× more CE than others) → a specific DIMM is failing, surface "csrow 3 channel A (DIMM_B0) has 47 corrected errors vs ~0 on others — replace that DIMM". Walk `/sys/devices/system/edac/mc/mc*/` once (typically 1-2 memory controllers per box), per-mc read `ce_count` / `ue_count` / `size_mb` / `seconds_since_reset` / `mc_name` / `max_location`, enumerate `csrow*/` subdirs (per-channel rows) read `ch*_ce_count` + `ch*_dimm_label` + `size_mb` + `edac_mode` (`SECDED` / `S4ECD4ED` / `none` / `R-DDR-SECDED` for registered) + `mem_type` (DDR4 / DDR5 / RDIMM / LRDIMM), enumerate `dimm*/` subdirs (per-DIMM stats on newer kernels) read `dimm_label` + `dimm_location` + `size` + `dimm_dev_type` + `dimm_mem_type`, cross-reference with `/sys/devices/virtual/dmi/id/{board_name,sys_vendor}` (shipped `dmi_bios.py` + `host_class.py`) for board-specific ECC support hints, shipped #buddyinfo_frag (ECC retirements degrade buddy zones), shipped #ecc_remap (GPU-side counterpart), classify into 5 verdicts: (a) ECC active + all `ce_count=0` + uptime > 24 h → ECC healthy, congratulate, (b) ECC active + `ce_count > 0` but distributed across DIMMs evenly → background cosmic ray rate, monitor, (c) ECC active + one specific csrow/DIMM has >5× the CE of others → that DIMM is failing, paste-ready DIMM-swap recipe with label, (d) ECC active + `ue_count > 0` ever this boot → silent corruption already happened, cross-link to shipped #nvrm_tail + dmesg MCE search, advise full memtest + log archival, (e) `mc/` empty or absent → no ECC, surface "your inference workload runs on consumer DRAM with no bit-flip protection, ~1 silent bit-flip per ~10-100 GB-h of RAM activity = ~1 per ~1-10 days on a 32-GB box; this is invisible and explains a slice of 'why does llama sometimes hallucinate worse on this box'" + recommend ECC upgrade path (Ryzen Pro / Threadripper Pro / EPYC). Surface "your AM5 7950X with 64 GB DDR5 ECC: edac driver `amd64_edac` loaded, mc0 reports 0 CE / 0 UE / 168 hours uptime, all 4 DIMMs labelled (A0/A1/B0/B1) at `S4ECD4ED` mode → ECC healthy, you are protected against single-bit silent corruption — keep monitoring". Niche but extremely-high-leverage feature for the slice of audience that bought ECC RAM (Ryzen Pro / Threadripper / EPYC + ECC UDIMMs) and got nothing in their dashboard showing it works, *and* for the slice that thought their AM5 board "supported ECC" (vendor marketing trap: Asus B650-Creator and similar advertise "ECC support" but in practice BIOS-default-disabled or kernel-sees-non-ECC) who learn their silent-corruption exposure for the first time. Sibling to shipped `ecc_remap.py` (GPU side) for the complete "every bit-flip-prone substrate in this box is monitored" picture. First : `modules/edac_ram_ecc.py` + GET `/api/edac-ram-ecc`. |
| 41.3 | **`/proc/sys/kernel/{panic,panic_on_oops,panic_on_warn,panic_on_io_nmi,panic_on_unrecovered_nmi,hung_task_panic,hung_task_timeout_secs,hung_task_warnings,softlockup_panic,softlockup_all_cpu_backtrace,hardlockup_panic,nmi_watchdog,oops_limit,warn_limit}` + `/sys/kernel/{kexec_loaded,kexec_crash_loaded}` headless-rig auto-reboot + hang-detection policy auditor** | XS | 5 | A headless inference rig running 24/7 in a closet (the dominant homelab pattern) has *no console, no monitor, nobody watching it* — and when llama-server triggers a kernel oops (rare but happens with marginal PCIe AER + nvidia DMA misalignment) or a `khungtaskd`-detected hang on the GPU IRQ thread, the *only* difference between "automatic reboot, back online in 90 s" and "wedged for 14 h until I notice the Home Assistant integration is dead" is a handful of `/proc/sys/kernel/{panic,hung_task_*,softlockup_*}` knobs that ship with widely-different defaults across distros. The recurring foot-guns: (1) `kernel.panic=0` (Ubuntu / Debian default) → on a panic the kernel halts forever waiting for a human to press a button, on a headless rig this is catastrophic — `kernel.panic=10` reboots after 10 s, (2) `kernel.panic_on_oops=0` (default everywhere) → an oops (less severe than a panic) prints a stack trace and continues, but the system is now in an undefined state where shipped #kernel_taint flags it as tainted — on a headless rig you actively *want* `panic_on_oops=1` to escalate-then-reboot rather than limp with corrupted kernel state, (3) `kernel.hung_task_timeout_secs=120` (Ubuntu/Fedora default) + `hung_task_panic=0` → if any task hangs in D-state for 2 minutes (an inference worker stuck on a GPU PCIe AER recovery, an NVMe-swap pageout stalled on a degrading SSD) the kernel logs a stack trace to dmesg but does *not* reboot, the rig hangs silently — recommend `hung_task_panic=1` + `hung_task_timeout_secs=60` for headless rigs, (4) `kernel.softlockup_panic=0` (default) → a softlockup (one CPU stuck in kernel mode for >20 s, typical of GPU IRQ-storm cascade) prints a warning and continues, recommend `softlockup_panic=1`, (5) `kernel.nmi_watchdog=1` enabled but `hardlockup_panic=0` → NMI fires on hardlockup detection but kernel doesn't reboot, (6) `kernel.panic_on_warn=0` (default) → kernel WARN_ON() output (nvidia.ko emits these on driver bugs) is logged and ignored, on a flaky-driver rig you can want WARN_ON to escalate, (7) `kexec_crash_loaded=0` → no crash kernel armed, the panic reboot will not produce a kdump, you'll have nothing to post-mortem, recommend `kdump-tools` install + kexec crash kernel pre-loaded for actual root-cause capture, (8) `oops_limit` / `warn_limit` (kernel ≥ 6.2) — kernel hardening that escalates to panic after N oopses (default 10000) — homelab users with a flaky GPU may want this lower to force a clean reboot faster. Read all ~15 knobs from `/proc/sys/kernel/*`, plus `/sys/kernel/{kexec_loaded,kexec_crash_loaded,fadump_enabled}`, cross-reference shipped #kernel_taint (taint history), #nvrm_tail (XID + dmesg log), #hw_watchdog (hardware watchdog is the *physical* layer of the same story), #watchdog_setup, #host_class (skip on container guests), shipped #39.4-equivalent `host_class.py` (form-factor: a desktop with a monitor wants different defaults than a headless server), classify into 4 posture profiles: (a) Desktop / Monitor Attached (`kernel.panic=0` + `panic_on_oops=0` + `hung_task_panic=0`) = sane default, human will see the crash, no advice, (b) Headless Production Default → recommend `kernel.panic=10` + `kernel.panic_on_oops=1` + `kernel.hung_task_timeout_secs=60` + `kernel.hung_task_panic=1` + `kernel.softlockup_panic=1` + paste-ready `/etc/sysctl.d/99-llm-headless-panic.conf` snippet (interacts cleanly with shipped `sysctl_d_audit.py` for drift-protection), (c) Aggressive Recovery (the above + `kdump-tools` install + kexec crash kernel pre-loaded) for power-user rigs that want post-mortems, (d) "I want it to never reboot because I'm developing kernel modules" override (acknowledge intent). Surface "your llama-server rig has `kernel.panic=0` (Ubuntu default) + `hung_task_panic=0`: when your nvidia.ko emits a XID 13 + softlockup tomorrow at 3 AM, the kernel will print to dmesg and hang forever — the dashboard webserver will time out, Home Assistant will mark your integration unavailable, and you'll restart it manually Wednesday morning. Drop the snippet below into `/etc/sysctl.d/99-llm-headless-panic.conf` for automatic recovery in 10-30 s — paste-ready" + paste-ready hw_watchdog cross-link (shipped #hw_watchdog is the *out-of-band* layer if the kernel itself dies before the panic timeout). Tiniest scope (~15 file reads + 4 profile branches), biggest "explains why my rig was offline for 14 h on Saturday" payoff for the headless homelab audience (~70 % of the user base). Pairs with shipped `kernel_taint.py`, `hw_watchdog.py`, `watchdog_setup.py`, `nvrm_tail.py`, just-shipped `sysctl_d_audit.py` (for the new `99-llm-headless-panic.conf` drift-protection). First : `modules/panic_policy.py` + GET `/api/panic-policy`. |
| 41.4 | **`/proc/sys/fs/inotify/{max_user_watches,max_user_instances,max_queued_events}` + `/proc/<pid>/fdinfo/<fd>` inotify+fanotify watch-descriptor inventory + ollama/lm-studio/jupyter watcher-exhaustion auditor** | S | 4 | Modern inference rigs accumulate filesystem watchers like compound interest: ollama watches `~/.ollama/models/` for new GGUFs, LM Studio watches `~/.cache/lm-studio/models/` + `~/Documents/`, Jupyter watches the active notebook's cwd for autoreload, every code editor (VS Code, Cursor, Helix) watches the open project tree, `systemd-tmpfiles` watches `/tmp`, MangoHud / GameMode watch their config dirs, the Hugging Face cache cleaner watches `~/.cache/huggingface/hub/`, the dashboard itself watches `/sys/class/drm/card0/device/{power_state,current_link_speed}` via inotify — and every Linux distro ships `fs.inotify.max_user_watches=8192` (Ubuntu/Debian default) which is *catastrophically low* for the inference-rig pattern. The recurring foot-guns: (1) ollama silently fails to detect a freshly-downloaded GGUF because inotify added the 8193rd watcher and got ENOSPC, user reports "ollama list doesn't show the model I just `ollama pull`'d", real cause is inotify-watch exhaustion not ollama, (2) VS Code with a 50K-file project + ollama + LM Studio + Cursor all running → `max_user_instances=128` is hit (each app gets ~1 inotify instance per process, on a 16-Cursor-tab + 8-VS-Code-window box you can hit 128 fast), new watchers silently fail, (3) `max_queued_events=16384` overflowed → IN_Q_OVERFLOW event raised, inotify-aware programs respond by re-scanning entire trees (200ms-2s pause), on a busy build directory this is a *latency* foot-gun not a *correctness* one, (4) per-PID inotify-watcher leak: a buggy Python script using `watchdog` library that never calls `.stop()` accumulates watchers until process exit — `/proc/<pid>/fdinfo/<inotify-fd>` lists every watch descriptor, count them per-PID to surface the leak, (5) Docker / Podman containers each see the host's inotify limits (namespaced since 5.11 but most distros still expose host values to containers) — running 8 ollama containers on Proxmox VE with each watching its own model dir easily blows past host `max_user_watches`, surface the cross-namespace pressure, (6) `fanotify` (newer API, supports IN_PERMISSION + access control) — `fs.fanotify.max_user_marks` + `max_user_groups` + `max_queued_events` are typically 8192 / 128 / 16384 (mirror of inotify), used by `systemd-journald` for log-rotation + antivirus + some sandboxing — exhaust the same way silently. Today shipped `proc_static_audit.py` covers static `/proc/sys/*` knobs broadly but doesn't surface inotify limit pressure or per-PID watcher counts. Read `/proc/sys/fs/inotify/{max_user_watches,max_user_instances,max_queued_events}` + `/proc/sys/fs/fanotify/{max_user_marks,max_user_groups,max_queued_events}`, walk shipped service-discovery PIDs (ollama, llama-server, lm-studio, jupyter, vllm, comfyui, koboldcpp) + the user's top-RSS GUI apps (cursor, code, helix), per-PID enumerate `/proc/<pid>/fd/*` symlinks looking for `anon_inode:inotify` / `anon_inode:[fanotify]`, then read `/proc/<pid>/fdinfo/<fd>` for the inotify case (lists every watch descriptor as `wd:<id> ino:<ino> sdev:<sdev> mask:<events> ignored_mask:<mask> fhandle-bytes:<n> fhandle-type:<n> f_handle:<hex>`), count watchers per PID + per filesystem, classify into 4 pressure verdicts: (a) `max_user_watches=8192` (Ubuntu default) + active inotify-using PIDs at <50 % utilization → headroom OK, congratulate, (b) `max_user_watches=8192` + ollama PID has >2000 watchers + projected growth from HF-cache → headed for ENOSPC within hours/days, recommend bump to 524288 with paste-ready `/etc/sysctl.d/99-llm-inotify.conf` snippet (interacts with shipped sysctl_d_audit), (c) one PID has 10× more watchers than its peers (leak symptom) → flag the leaker with PID + cmdline, (d) IN_Q_OVERFLOW seen in dmesg (`grep -i 'inotify' /proc/<pid>/limits`) → events dropping, latency hits. Surface "your `fs.inotify.max_user_watches=8192` (Ubuntu default), ollama PID 12834 has 2847 watchers + lm-studio PID 14201 has 3122 + cursor PID 18934 has 1893 = 7862 used of 8192 (96 %); next `ollama pull` will hit ENOSPC and fail silently — bump to 524288 with `/etc/sysctl.d/99-llm-inotify.conf`: `fs.inotify.max_user_watches = 524288` (~64 MB kernel RAM at full saturation), paste-ready snippet below" + cross-link to shipped `sysctl_d_audit.py` for drift-protection of the new file. Niche but high-frequency-of-being-the-actual-root-cause feature: catches the silent "why doesn't ollama see my model" / "why does VS Code stop highlighting files" / "why is Jupyter autoreload broken" complaint cluster that today nothing on Linux surfaces cleanly with a per-PID breakdown. Pairs with shipped `service_discovery.py` (inference PIDs), `proc_static_audit.py` (sibling sysctl knobs), just-shipped `sysctl_d_audit.py` (persistence). First : `modules/inotify_audit.py` + GET `/api/inotify-audit`. |
| 41.5 | **`/sys/firmware/efi/efivars/{Boot*-*,BootOrder-*,SecureBoot-*,SetupMode-*,PK-*,KEK-*,db-*,dbx-*}` + `/sys/firmware/efi/mok-list-{rt,xrt}` UEFI / Secure Boot / MOK key inventory + nvidia-signed-module readiness auditor** | M | 4 | Modern homelab boards (AM5, X670E, B650E, LGA1700 Z790, TRX50, sTR5) ship with Secure Boot on by default since ~2023, and Linux's nvidia kernel module requires either (a) a signed proprietary driver from a vendor-provided signing key (Ubuntu HWE / RHEL kernel module signing service), (b) the user has manually enrolled their own MOK (Machine Owner Key) and signed nvidia.ko with it, or (c) Secure Boot is off. Today shipped `dkms_status.py` checks DKMS-rebuilt module status, shipped `kernel_taint.py` flags G/E/X taints — but neither walks `/sys/firmware/efi/efivars/` to surface "your Secure Boot is ON, your kernel is signed, your nvidia.ko is from DKMS without MOK enrollment, on next kernel update the driver will silently fail to load and `nvidia-smi` will say 'No devices were found' until the user notices and re-enrolls MOK". The recurring foot-guns: (1) Secure Boot ON + nvidia-driver from `apt install nvidia-driver-550` (Ubuntu HWE flavor, ships pre-signed by Canonical's signing key in `db`) → works out of the box, congratulate, (2) Secure Boot ON + nvidia-driver from DKMS rebuild (550.x DKMS .run installer, user's own build) → requires `mokutil --import /var/lib/dkms/mok.pub` + reboot + MOK menu confirmation → if the user hasn't done step 3, after next kernel upgrade the nvidia.ko is silently rejected, flag this BEFORE the next `apt upgrade linux-image-*` happens, (3) Secure Boot OFF + MOK keys still enrolled → harmless but surface "Secure Boot off, MOK enrollment is now no-op, you can remove the MOK key with `mokutil --delete <key>`", (4) `db` (signature database) missing Microsoft UEFI CA → user shimmed in their own key but lost Microsoft's, third-party OS-bootloader media won't work, (5) `dbx` (revocation list) outdated → kernel/shim are signed by a revoked key, system won't boot on next Secure Boot policy update, (6) `BootOrder` non-deterministic across reboots (a known firmware bug on Asus X670E rev1 boards + some MSI Z790 BIOS) — surface as "your Boot0001/Boot0002 ordering changed between last 3 reboots", (7) `SetupMode=1` (user has Secure Boot in "Setup mode" with PK cleared) → anyone with root can enroll any key, full custom-CA setup ready but probably not intentional, surface clearly, (8) `BootCurrent` does not match `Boot0001` in `BootOrder` → an EFI boot manager (rEFInd, systemd-boot) has overridden, surface for transparency. Read `/sys/firmware/efi/efivars/` (each file is `<name>-<vendor-guid>`, first 4 bytes are attributes (NV/RT/BS), remaining is binary EFI variable data — parse with stdlib `struct` per UEFI spec § 8.2 + § 32.4), specifically decode: `SecureBoot-<guid>` (1 byte, 0=off, 1=on), `SetupMode-<guid>` (1 byte), `BootCurrent-<guid>` (uint16 LE = active boot entry number), `BootOrder-<guid>` (array of uint16 LE = boot order), each `Boot<XXXX>-<guid>` (EFI_LOAD_OPTION struct: attributes uint32, file_path_list_length uint16, description UTF-16 null-terminated, file_path_list = EFI device path), `PK-<guid>` (Platform Key, presence + size only — don't try to parse X.509 fully, just count), `KEK-<guid>` (Key Exchange Keys, count), `db-<guid>` (signature database, count entries), `dbx-<guid>` (forbidden signatures, count entries — empty means no revocations seen, common but worth surfacing on a Win11+SB box), `/sys/firmware/efi/mok-list-rt` + `/sys/firmware/efi/mok-list-xrt` (MOK key list — count enrolled keys, decode common name field if straightforward), cross-reference shipped `dkms_status.py` (DKMS build state), `kernel_taint.py` (unsigned-module taint flag G), `dmi_bios.py` (board/BIOS vendor for known-buggy boards), `host_class.py` (skip on KVM guest — EFI may be passthrough OVMF without these), classify into 6 posture verdicts: (a) Secure Boot OFF + nvidia loaded + no MOK → development box, no advice, (b) Secure Boot ON + nvidia from distro-signed package + kernel-taint G absent → optimal, congratulate, (c) Secure Boot ON + DKMS-built nvidia + MOK pubkey not in `mok-list-rt` → DANGER, next kernel upgrade will silently break nvidia.ko, paste-ready `mokutil --import /var/lib/dkms/mok.pub` + "reboot, enter MOK menu, confirm" recipe, (d) Secure Boot ON + DKMS-built + MOK enrolled → optimal for power user, congratulate, (e) `SetupMode=1` + `SecureBoot=0` → board in setup mode, full custom-CA possible, surface intentional-or-not, (f) `BootOrder` changed between reboots → known-buggy-firmware behavior, flag with board vendor + paste-ready `efibootmgr -o 0001,0002,…` recipe to re-pin order. Surface "your AM5 7950X has Secure Boot ON, nvidia.ko is from `apt install nvidia-driver-555` (Canonical-signed, present in `db-<guid>` as `Canonical Ltd. Master Certificate Authority`), MOK not enrolled (no DKMS pubkey present), `kernel-taint=0` → optimal, next kernel upgrade will keep nvidia working" or "your X670E + DKMS nvidia 555.42: Secure Boot ON, MOK pubkey at `/var/lib/dkms/mok.pub` is NOT in `mok-list-rt` — next kernel upgrade will silently break nvidia.ko, run `sudo mokutil --import /var/lib/dkms/mok.pub` now, reboot, then in the MOK menu choose `Enroll MOK → Continue → Yes → enter password` to enrol — paste-ready recipe + screenshot description". Effort is M because UEFI variable parsing requires careful binary handling + EFI_LOAD_OPTION + EFI device path decoding, but stdlib `struct` + `codecs` (UTF-16) suffice, no extra deps. Niche but extremely-high-payoff: catches the "after `apt upgrade` my GPU stopped working" silent-rejection that hits a meaningful slice of Secure-Boot-default users every ~6 months at kernel-version bumps. Pairs with shipped `dkms_status.py`, `kernel_taint.py`, `dmi_bios.py`, `host_class.py` (form-factor: KVM-guest EFI is different), shipped #29.1 kmod_params (nvidia.ko params). First : `modules/efi_secureboot.py` + GET `/api/efi-secureboot`. |
| 41.6 | **`/proc/zoneinfo` + `/proc/pagetypeinfo` per-zone watermark + per-migratetype fragmentation deep-dive (extends shipped `buddyinfo_frag.py` from buddy-only to full zone+migratetype picture)** | S | 4 | Shipped `buddyinfo_frag.py` parses `/proc/buddyinfo` for per-order free-page counts per zone — a snapshot of allocator fragmentation. But the kernel exposes *two* deeper sibling files that no shipped module reads: (1) `/proc/zoneinfo` lists, per-zone, the *watermarks* (min/low/high) the kernel uses to trigger kswapd wake / direct reclaim / OOM kill (the exact watermark values that #vm_tuning_deep's `watermark_scale_factor` advice tunes), the *protection* array (per-zone reserve floor below which higher-zone allocations can't dip into this zone), and a dozen `nr_*` counters (`nr_free_pages`, `nr_zone_active_anon`, `nr_zone_inactive_file`, `nr_writeback`, `nr_unstable`, `nr_pages_scanned`, `compact_*` counters) that together tell you "is this zone under pressure right now? is kswapd active? is direct reclaim hitting it? is compaction failing?"; (2) `/proc/pagetypeinfo` decomposes free pages *per migratetype* (Unmovable, Reclaimable, Movable, HighAtomic, CMA, Isolate) per zone per order — the missing dimension that says "you have 50 GB free total but the unmovable-migratetype is fragmented at order ≥ 9 so a kernel-stack 16-page contiguous alloc will fail and trigger compaction stalls". The recurring foot-guns the audit catches: (1) `nr_free_pages` near or below `low` watermark + non-zero `nr_pages_scanned` → direct reclaim active, inference t/s will stutter for 50-500 ms hiccups, surface as live pressure, (2) `protection: 0 0 8192 8192` mismatched with allocation pattern (DMA32 zone over-protected vs Normal) → kernel won't fall through Normal→DMA32 even under pressure, a relic of `lowmem_reserve_ratio` defaults that's actively wrong on 32-GB-host configs with a giant Normal zone, surface with tuning recipe, (3) `compact_success` flat + `compact_fail` incrementing → compaction is failing repeatedly, the Movable migratetype is exhausted, future huge-page allocations will fall back to smalls and shipped #thp_audit's khugepaged story degrades, (4) `Unmovable` migratetype fragmented at order ≥ 4 → kernel-side allocations (network skbuff pools, slab caches) will fail their fast path and stall, common after weeks of uptime on a busy box, (5) `HighAtomic` migratetype unusually large (>2 % of zone) → kernel reserving high-order atomic pages aggressively, symptom of frequent GFP_ATOMIC fail-spirals (often nvidia.ko DMA buffer alloc under interrupt context), worth surfacing as a clue when shipped #nvrm_tail logs alloc-fail XIDs, (6) `nr_isolated_anon` + `nr_isolated_file` non-zero stably → migration in progress for a long period, NUMA balancer is shuffling pages between nodes (shipped #35.3 numa_placement context), surface as live evidence of the balancer's work. Parse `/proc/zoneinfo` (whitespace-keyed lines per zone), `/proc/pagetypeinfo` (table format), cross-reference shipped `buddyinfo_frag.py` (free-page-per-order) + #vm_tuning_deep (watermark_scale_factor tuning) + #35.3 numa_placement (per-NUMA-node zones) + #31.1 thp_audit (THP requires high-order Movable), classify into 5 verdicts: (a) all zones healthy, watermarks far from low, no direct reclaim, no compaction failures → optimal, (b) Normal zone hovering near `low` watermark + active direct reclaim → memory pressure, surface "your llama-server pushed total RAM to 28.2 GB of 32 GB, Normal zone is at low watermark (`nr_free=12 MB`), kswapd is actively reclaiming, expect 50-200 ms hiccups during context-window growth", (c) Unmovable migratetype fragmented + atomic alloc fails in dmesg → fragmentation hit, recommend `echo 1 > /proc/sys/vm/compact_memory` immediate compaction + scheduled `vm.compaction_proactiveness=20` (kernel ≥ 5.7) drop-in for ongoing maintenance, (d) HighAtomic >2 % → nvidia.ko alloc-pressure indicator, cross-link shipped #nvrm_tail for alloc-fail XID search, (e) `protection` array mismatched with usage pattern → bump or drop `lowmem_reserve_ratio`. Surface "your Normal zone (28.4 GB) has 7.2 GB free total but only 12 MB at order ≥ 4 in the Unmovable migratetype after 18 days uptime → kernel-side high-order allocations will stall on compaction, run `echo 1 | sudo tee /proc/sys/vm/compact_memory` for an immediate one-shot compaction, then drop `vm.compaction_proactiveness=20` into `/etc/sysctl.d/99-llm-compaction.conf` for ongoing background compaction (kernel ≥ 5.7) — paste-ready snippet, interacts with just-shipped sysctl_d_audit". Niche but extremely-high-precision diagnostic for the "my 32-GB box was fine on day 1 and stalls on day 30" complaint that today nothing surfaces with the migratetype dimension. Pairs with shipped `buddyinfo_frag.py` (sibling, free-page-per-order baseline), shipped #vm_tuning_deep (the tuning side), shipped #35.3 numa_placement (per-node zones), shipped #thp_audit (THP allocation path). First : `modules/zoneinfo_pressure.py` + GET `/api/zoneinfo-pressure`. |
| 41.7 | **`/sys/devices/system/cpu/intel_uncore_frequency/package_*_die_*/{min_freq_khz,max_freq_khz,initial_min_freq_khz,initial_max_freq_khz,current_freq_khz}` Intel uncore-frequency tuner for inference-bound memory-bandwidth ceiling (Sapphire Rapids / Granite Rapids / Alder/Raptor/Meteor Lake)** | XS | 3 | On modern Intel platforms (Alder Lake 12th gen onwards client, Sapphire Rapids onwards server), the *uncore* (the LLC + ring-bus + memory-controller fabric, separate from the per-core P-states) has its own DVFS controlled by the kernel `intel_uncore_frequency` driver at `/sys/devices/system/cpu/intel_uncore_frequency/package_*_die_*/` — and on every BIOS-default-power-policy box the uncore floats between ~800 MHz idle and ~3.6-4.4 GHz turbo, with the kernel's HWP autonomously tuning *based on CPU load*. The problem for inference: a llama-server worker pinned to 8 cores at 100 % load *does* push the per-core P-states to max, but during the *tensor-load phase* (CPU streams ~24 GB GGUF off NVMe through the LLC into core's L1 in ~150 ms bursts) the *uncore* never sees the per-core demand because the per-core counters aren't pegged — and the kernel keeps the uncore at 1.2-2.0 GHz, capping the LLC↔memory-controller bandwidth at ~120 GB/s instead of the platform's ~80-100 GB/s ceiling, costing ~10-25 % t/s on the prompt-prefill phase of large prompts (4K+ tokens). The recurring foot-guns: (1) `intel_uncore_frequency` driver not loaded (kernel < 5.6 or `intel_uncore_frequency=off`) → can't tune, surface "your kernel `<version>` doesn't expose uncore tuning, upgrade to ≥ 5.6 for this feature" — but on a modern homelab this is rare, (2) driver loaded but `min_freq_khz == initial_min_freq_khz` and `max_freq_khz == initial_max_freq_khz` (BIOS defaults still in place) → recommend writing `max_freq_khz` to the platform max for `min_freq_khz` (effectively pinning uncore at max) during inference workloads, ~5-15 % t/s improvement on prefill-bound prompts at +8-20 W idle cost, (3) user has *lowered* `max_freq_khz` below `initial_max_freq_khz` (probably from a copy-pasted "low-power tuning" guide) → flag the unintentional cap, (4) multi-package box (Sapphire Rapids dual-socket workstation, rare but possible on homelab eBay budgets) where only one package's uncore is tuned → recommend uniform tuning across packages, (5) `current_freq_khz` reading <50 % of `max_freq_khz` during active inference (the live measurement) → uncore is autonomously throttled despite headroom, evidence for tuning, (6) AMD Zen with the parallel `amd_pstate_epp` exposing `boost_max_perf` via `/sys/devices/system/cpu/cpufreq/policy*/` — *not* the same as uncore (Zen's "Infinity Fabric Clock" is BIOS-only on most boards, not Linux-tunable) but surface "AMD users: your IF clock is BIOS-side, see `cpufreq/policy*/boost` for boost-time tuning" as a fairness disclaimer. Read `/sys/devices/system/cpu/intel_uncore_frequency/` (each `package_X_die_Y/` subdir = one uncore domain), per-domain read `initial_min_freq_khz` / `initial_max_freq_khz` (BIOS-set platform bounds), `min_freq_khz` / `max_freq_khz` (current kernel-driver setpoints), `current_freq_khz` (live readback, kernel ≥ 5.18), cross-reference shipped #36.4 hwp_epp (per-core HWP-EPP string), #35.1 cpu_boost (turbo gate), shipped parked #40.7-equivalent (cpufreq domain map, not yet shipped) + shipped #37.4 cpu_cache_topology (L3 islands = uncore domains on tile-based CPUs), shipped #host_class (skip on KVM guest — uncore not exposed under passthrough), classify into 4 verdicts: (a) `intel_uncore_frequency` driver not present → not applicable (AMD, ARM, old Intel) — surface fairness note, (b) driver present + `min_freq_khz == initial_min_freq_khz` + active inference detected via shipped service_discovery → recommend uncore-pin-to-max during inference, paste-ready systemd Drop-In with `ExecStartPre=echo $(cat /sys/.../package_0_die_0/initial_max_freq_khz) > /sys/.../package_0_die_0/min_freq_khz` (raises floor to ceiling, effectively pins), (c) user already pinned → optimal, congratulate, (d) user lowered `max_freq_khz` → flag with one-shot reset recipe. Surface "your 14900K has uncore @ package_0_die_0: initial_min=800 MHz, initial_max=3600 MHz, current_min=800 MHz, current_max=3600 MHz, live current_freq=2200 MHz under llama-server load → uncore is throttling to ~61 % of platform max during inference; pin floor to max with `echo 3600000 > /sys/devices/system/cpu/intel_uncore_frequency/package_0_die_0/min_freq_khz` for ~8-15 % t/s on prefill-heavy prompts (cost: ~12 W extra idle). Paste-ready systemd Drop-In below to apply on `llama-server.service` start + revert on stop". Niche audience (Intel-only homelabbers, ~30-40 % of audience), but extremely-high-precision tuning for the prefill-bound inference pattern (large prompts, RAG, code-completion with long context). Pairs with shipped #36.4 hwp_epp (per-core HWP EPP), #35.1 cpu_boost (turbo gate), #37.4 cpu_cache_topology (uncore-domain map), #service_discovery (active inference detection), #host_class (skip on virt). First : `modules/intel_uncore_freq.py` + GET `/api/intel-uncore-freq`. |
| 41.8 | **`/proc/keys` + `/proc/key-users` + `/sys/kernel/security/integrity/ima/{policy,ascii_runtime_measurements}` kernel-keyring + IMA-policy inventory for module-signing + DM-Verity + cryptsetup key audit** | M | 3 | The Linux kernel keyring (`/proc/keys`, `/proc/key-users`) holds every cryptographic key the kernel currently has loaded: nvidia.ko's module-signing key (`.builtin_trusted_keys` ring), MOK enrolled keys (`.platform` ring on kernel ≥ 5.4), DM-Verity root hashes for the user's rootfs (`_uid.0` if `verity` mounts), cryptsetup LUKS volume keys (`logon` keys for `dm-crypt`), kerberos session tickets (rare on homelab but seen on AD-joined boxes), and the IMA (Integrity Measurement Architecture) policy at `/sys/kernel/security/integrity/ima/policy` decides which file accesses get measured (hash-recorded into TPM PCR 10) and which get verified-against-stored-hash. Today *nothing* in the shipped stack surfaces the kernel keyring at all — and the audience that cares (security-conscious homelabbers who want their inference rig to also be a hardened secret-holder for, say, an LLM that processes private documents) has no answer to "what keys does my kernel currently trust, what files does it measure into TPM, and is my nvidia.ko being verified against a key I control?". The recurring foot-guns: (1) `keyctl show @us` shows zero session-level keys for the `dashboard` user → no per-user keyring quota, fine, but worth surfacing for transparency, (2) `_module_signing_key` present in `.builtin_trusted_keys` (kernel ≥ 5.4) → kernel was built with `CONFIG_MODULE_SIG_KEY=` and trusts its own per-build key, paired with shipped #41.5 efi-secureboot for the full chain-of-trust picture, (3) `.platform` keyring contains MOK keys after kernel ≥ 5.4 (the in-kernel side of MOK enrollment) — count them, surface counts, (4) IMA policy file is empty (default: no measurement) → IMA disabled, no integrity-attestation possible for this kernel, common on consumer Ubuntu/Fedora, (5) IMA policy file has rules but `ascii_runtime_measurements` is also non-empty → measurements being recorded, surface what's measured (typically `boot_aggregate` + every executable + every kernel module), (6) `key-users` shows non-zero `quota_keys` / `quota_bytes` for the dashboard's UID → quota near limit, surface, (7) `/sys/kernel/security/integrity/{evm,ima}/*` reveal whether EVM (Extended Verification Module) is active — almost never on homelab, but if it is and the user pasted a config from a guide without understanding, surface clearly, (8) cryptsetup `logon` keys for dm-crypt → indicates LUKS-encrypted rootfs / data partition active, useful for cross-correlating "my llama-server reads `/data/models/llama-70b.gguf` from an LUKS-encrypted volume, surface that's protected at rest". Read `/proc/keys` (whitespace-separated table: serial number, flags, usage count, timeout, permissions, UID, GID, type, description), `/proc/key-users` (per-UID: nkeys, nikeys, qnkeys/maxkeys, qnbytes/maxbytes), `/sys/kernel/security/integrity/ima/policy` (multi-line policy rules, may need root to read), `/sys/kernel/security/integrity/ima/ascii_runtime_measurements` (TPM-PCR-10 measurement log, lines like `10 <hash> ima-ng sha256:<file-hash> <path>`), cross-reference shipped #41.5 efi-secureboot (companion EFI-side chain of trust), shipped `kernel_taint.py` (unsigned-module taint flag G), `dkms_status.py` (DKMS signing pipeline), `kmod_params.py` (nvidia params), `host_class.py` (skip on container guest — keyring is namespaced), classify into 4 posture verdicts: (a) `.builtin_trusted_keys` populated + `.platform` MOK keys present + IMA off + LUKS active → standard hardened-desktop posture, congratulate, (b) `_module_signing_key` absent + Secure Boot on + unsigned-taint G present → broken module-signing chain, cross-link to shipped #41.5 + DKMS recipe, (c) IMA policy active + measurements logging → security-aware setup, surface what's being measured (top 10 files by frequency in `ascii_runtime_measurements`) for transparency, (d) keyring quota near limit for any UID → flag with `keyctl reap` recipe. Surface "your kernel keyring has 47 keys: `.builtin_trusted_keys` (4 keys: kernel-self-signing + Canonical CA + 2 module-signing CAs), `.platform` MOK ring (2 keys: nvidia-DKMS + custom userland-CA), no IMA measurement active, dm-crypt logon keys for 2 LUKS volumes (/dev/dm-0 = root, /dev/dm-1 = /data) → module-signing chain intact, your rootfs and /data are encrypted at rest; if you want to enable IMA measurement for tamper-detection on critical inference binaries, paste the policy below into `/etc/ima/ima-policy` + reboot — paste-ready policy snippet measures ollama, llama-server, vllm, jupyter, plus `/etc/sysctl.d/*` and `/etc/modprobe.d/*`". Effort is M because IMA policy parsing + key-type-specific description decoding (`asymmetric:` keys have CN-encoded descriptions, `logon:` keys are opaque hex) requires careful handling, but stdlib `re` + `struct` suffice. Very niche audience (the security-aware sub-slice of homelabbers — ~5-8 % of audience), but the cleanest "your inference rig's chain-of-trust from EFI boot → kernel → modules → mounted data is fully mapped" feature in the entire stack for that slice. Pairs with shipped #41.5 efi-secureboot (EFI side), shipped `kernel_taint.py` (taint), `dkms_status.py`, `kmod_params.py`. First : `modules/keyring_ima_audit.py` + GET `/api/keyring-ima-audit`. |

**Top 4 (fit × urgency)** :
1. 41.1 zswap + zram compressed-swap auditor — S, fit 5, the missing "your 32-GB host running a 24-GB-quant is one context-window-growth away from a 200-2000 µs NVMe-swap latency cliff, and the kernel has a built-in compressed-RAM buffer that absorbs 60-80 % of that traffic at ~50 µs latency but it's off by default on every consumer Linux distro" diagnostic that today nothing in the shipped stack surfaces. Walks `/sys/module/zswap/parameters/*` (enabled / compressor / zpool / max_pool_percent / same_filled toggles) + `/sys/kernel/debug/zswap/*` (live compression ratio + reject counters) + `/sys/block/zram*/mm_stat` (per-zram disksize + comp_algorithm + orig vs compressed bytes) + `/proc/swaps` (active swap layers + priority order), classifies into 5 verdicts (optimal / zswap-disabled-on-tight-RAM / suboptimal-compressor / zram+zswap-conflict / misconfigured-same-filled), emits paste-ready GRUB cmdline snippet (zswap params are cmdline-time, not runtime — load-bearing detail that no quick-start guide gets right) with `zswap.enabled=1 zswap.compressor=lz4 zswap.zpool=zsmalloc zswap.max_pool_percent=40`. Pairs with shipped `nvme_swap.py` (backing layer), shipped #vm_tuning_deep (page-cluster + watermark), shipped #buddyinfo_frag (allocator fragmentation), shipped #service_discovery (which PID owns the giant mmap). Single highest-leverage feature for the RAM-tight + VRAM-rich audience (the dominant single-RTX-3090 homelab pattern, ~50-60 % of audience) that today no OSS Linux tool surfaces cleanly. First : `modules/zswap_zram_audit.py`.
2. 41.2 EDAC system-RAM ECC error-counter + DIMM-label auditor — XS, fit 5, the sibling-of-GPU-ECC feature the dashboard has been missing: shipped `ecc_remap.py` watches RTX 3090 VRAM ECC retirements, but says nothing about the system-RAM ECC layer that gates whether the *dequantised tensors in main RAM* are bit-flip-protected. Walks `/sys/devices/system/edac/mc/mc*/{ce_count,ue_count,csrow*/{ch*_ce_count,ch*_dimm_label},dimm*/{dimm_label,dimm_location,dimm_edac_mode}}` to surface per-DIMM correctable + uncorrectable error counts with the EDAC-exposed DIMM physical labels (`DIMM_A1` / `B0` / etc.), classifies into 5 verdicts (no-ECC-hardware / ECC-healthy / ECC-active-with-CE-distribution-skewed-to-one-DIMM / ECC-uncorrectable-historical / ECC-capable-but-BIOS-disabled). Cleanly handles the "you paid for ECC RAM on Asus B650-Creator but BIOS has it disabled by default" + "your csrow 3 has 47 corrected errors vs 0 elsewhere, replace DIMM_B0" foot-gun. Niche but extremely-high-leverage for the Ryzen Pro / Threadripper Pro / EPYC ECC slice + transparency for the consumer-DRAM slice ("you have NO ECC, every silent bit-flip will hit your inference workload"). Lowest-effort pick of the cycle: ~10 file reads + 5 verdict branches. Pairs with shipped `ecc_remap.py` (GPU side), shipped `dmi_bios.py` (board capability), shipped `host_class.py`. First : `modules/edac_ram_ecc.py`.
3. 41.3 headless-rig panic + hung_task + softlockup auto-reboot policy auditor — XS, fit 5, the missing "your headless inference rig will hang for 14 hours next time nvidia.ko emits a XID 13 + softlockup at 3 AM because Ubuntu's `kernel.panic=0` default has the kernel halt-forever on panic and nobody is watching the console" diagnostic that today no shipped module covers. Reads ~15 knobs from `/proc/sys/kernel/{panic,panic_on_oops,panic_on_warn,hung_task_panic,hung_task_timeout_secs,softlockup_panic,hardlockup_panic,nmi_watchdog,oops_limit,warn_limit}` + `/sys/kernel/{kexec_loaded,kexec_crash_loaded}`, cross-references shipped `host_class.py` (desktop-with-monitor vs headless-server form-factor dictates different defaults), shipped `kernel_taint.py` + `hw_watchdog.py` + `watchdog_setup.py` + `nvrm_tail.py`, classifies into 4 posture profiles (desktop-monitor-attached / headless-production / aggressive-recovery-with-kdump / development-override). Emits a paste-ready `/etc/sysctl.d/99-llm-headless-panic.conf` with `kernel.panic=10 + panic_on_oops=1 + hung_task_panic=1 + hung_task_timeout_secs=60 + softlockup_panic=1` that interacts cleanly with just-shipped `sysctl_d_audit.py` for drift-protection. Tiniest scope (~15 reads + 4 branches), biggest "explains why my rig was offline for 14 h on Saturday" payoff for the headless homelab audience (~70 % of user base). First : `modules/panic_policy.py`.
4. 41.4 inotify + fanotify watch-descriptor inventory + per-PID watcher-exhaustion auditor — S, fit 4, the missing "ollama silently dropped your freshly-pulled GGUF because `fs.inotify.max_user_watches=8192` (Ubuntu default) hit the ceiling between VS Code + LM Studio + Cursor + Jupyter + the HF cache cleaner" diagnostic that today nothing on Linux surfaces with a per-PID breakdown. Reads `/proc/sys/fs/inotify/{max_user_watches,max_user_instances,max_queued_events}` + `/proc/sys/fs/fanotify/*` for the limits side, then walks shipped service-discovery + GUI-app PIDs and enumerates `/proc/<pid>/fd/*` for `anon_inode:inotify` + reads `/proc/<pid>/fdinfo/<fd>` to count watch descriptors per PID + per filesystem, classifies into 4 pressure verdicts (headroom / near-ENOSPC / single-PID-leak / IN_Q_OVERFLOW-active). Catches the "why doesn't ollama see my new model" / "why is Jupyter autoreload broken" / "why does VS Code stop highlighting files" complaint cluster that all share inotify exhaustion as silent root cause. Paste-ready `/etc/sysctl.d/99-llm-inotify.conf` with `max_user_watches=524288` (~64 MB kernel RAM at saturation) interacts with just-shipped `sysctl_d_audit.py` for drift-protection. Pairs with shipped `service_discovery.py`, `proc_static_audit.py`, just-shipped `sysctl_d_audit.py`. First : `modules/inotify_audit.py`.

Bench (41.5 UEFI / Secure Boot / MOK key inventory + nvidia-signed-module readiness / 41.6 zoneinfo + pagetypeinfo per-migratetype fragmentation deep-dive / 41.7 Intel uncore-frequency tuner / 41.8 kernel keyring + IMA-policy inventory) for cycles after top 4 lands.
